Commentary

The Significance of the US Naval Exercise in the Pacific 28

— Ji

The six-week major exercise of the US Navy in the Pacific began on the 3rd of this month. More than 150 warships of various types and more than 400 aircraft participated in the exercise. Under the command of Navy Commander Reeves, they have all departed from their anchorages and set out into the open sea. The scope of the exercise extends from the Aleutian Islands in the north to Midway Island in the south, and to the coast of California in the east, forming a triangle that occupies approximately 5 million miles of sea surface. The vanguard team violates international borders. The scale is large, the plan is thorough, and the military is strong. According to Reeves, this is unprecedented in the history of the US Navy. At a time when the situation in the Pacific is tense, this move by the United States cannot be ignored.

The news of this major exercise by the US Navy in the Pacific was revealed before the failure of the first preparatory meeting for the London Naval Conference last year. In mid-September, US Secretary of the Navy Swanson publicly announced the matter. By the end of December last year, Japan openly declared its abandonment of the Washington Naval Treaty. US Navy Commander Reeves then announced his plan for an unprecedented major exercise in the Pacific. The major exercise of the US Navy is related to the failure of last year's preparatory meeting for the Naval Conference and Japan's abandonment of the Washington Naval Treaty.

The US Navy's fear of the Japanese fleet did not begin today. Last March, the US Senate and House of Representatives passed the Vinson Naval Act. In July of the same year, the Invincible Navy plan was proposed. A major naval battle exercise was held by the US fleet on both sides of the Panama Canal, using extraordinary means to prepare for the Panama Canal and the eastern United States. On April 19 of this year, Washington publicly announced three military plans in the Pacific. (1) The plan for the North Pacific aviation exercise. (2) To improve the various facilities of the army and navy in the Panama Canal and to study the issue of restricting railway staff in the canal zone to those with US citizenship, because Air Force Commander Colonel Cole had reported that a certain Asian country is currently using its instructors to train the Peruvian army. (3) To incorporate the flagship of the Asiatic Fleet, the USS Augusta, into the Combined Fleet and replace it with the light cruiser USS Omaha. This plan is the most striking. Otherwise, if war breaks out between Japan and the United States one day, the US Asiatic Fleet will be in danger of being sacrificed. Therefore, it is a wise strategy to use a fast light cruiser as a flagship. None of the above is not a move by the United States to prepare for a rainy day. US Secretary of the Navy Swanson said, "The reason why the US Navy chose the northern Pacific for this exercise is based on the policy of the Navy Department to familiarize the fleet with the coastal conditions there." It can be seen that the goal of the US Navy's major exercise is to correct its own weaknesses through simulated warfare in order to prepare for the crisis of future wars.

Therefore, the major exercise of the US Navy in the Pacific not only shows people that the US government has a heart to prepare for war, but also shows the US attitude towards the Pacific issue. Roosevelt's recovery plan has embarked on the path of overseas development. The so-called "good neighbor policy," the so-called "non-interventionism," and the so-called abandonment of the "open door" principle in the Far East, I am afraid, are nothing more than smoke bombs before its naval strength is sufficiently prepared.

(Tokyo) Ramos, the leader of the Philippine rural communist "Sakdalista" party, secretly arrived and went into hiding. Each wing carries small fighter planes, and its power is great enough to make the air forces of various countries feel chills in their hearts. This large bomber is equipped with two TB and small B and M engines, and the small planes installed on its left and right wings are the maximum-performance !·4 single-seat fighter planes. When the mother plane flies far into enemy territory to carry out bombing, it leaves its mother plane to prevent attacks from enemy fighter planes, allowing the mother plane to completely fulfill its bombing mission. The mother plane has a performance of 200 kilometers per hour, and a flight time of eight hours, while the child plane has a speed of 280 kilometers per hour, and a flight time of two hours. Therefore, within a distance of 500 kilometers, the mother and child three aircraft can return to their base after reaching their destination. Soviet Brain Disease Treatment Techniques 35

(Tashkent News Agency, Moscow Communication, April 4th) After the First World War, there were thousands of disabled people in the Soviet Union due to brain injuries. For several years, Moscow, Leningrad, Kharkov, Rostov and other places have established neurological sanatoriums, and are presided over by famous scholars Fedorov, Lorenov and others. The Moscow Central Neurological Disease Treatment Research Institute and the Moscow Medical Research Institute have completed approximately one thousand types of surgery for neurological diseases. Recently, a patient had a tumor growing in the left corner of his brain, weighing 200 grams, and its roots were very deep. After being cut, the process was very good. After more than ten days, the patient requested to be discharged from the hospital. Soviet technology in the treatment of neurological diseases is progressing day by day, so the international scientific community is paying close attention.

Although the Chairman is unable to come in person to instruct due to his supervision in Guizhou, all the plans decided by this conference must be submitted for approval and will be implemented gradually according to their urgency. In fact, it is no different from being guided by the Chairman. I hope that you will all continue to work hard after returning to your original agencies, carefully plan, and consult with the department in charge of the headquarters at any time to seek the rapid progress of our country's armaments construction cause." (6th Central News Agency telegram)

(Hankou) The Armaments Construction Conference of the headquarters closed on the 5th. Many important cases were resolved during the three-day meeting, especially the adoption of the outline of the implementation measures for armaments construction, which is a great contribution to the national construction cause. Ministry of Finance Implements Budget Settlement 43

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance's implementation of budget and settlement measures regarding the conclusion of revenue and expenditure matters has been agreed with the Directorate General of Budgets, Accounts and Statistics and will be extended to the end of May. Previously, the revenue and expenditure of various agencies before the end of the 22nd year were not handled in accordance with the budget and settlement. In order to seek fundamental remedies, the Ministry of Finance has formulated a conclusion method by the Directorate General of Budgets, Accounts and Statistics, and the National Government has issued an order to various agencies to uniformly conclude by the end of March of this year in accordance with this method. Because various agencies requested a one-month extension, it was extended to the end of April. However, due to procedural relationships, such as delays in review and compilation, it is estimated that all matters can be concluded by the end of May. Regarding the handling of the 22nd year settlement matters, it was originally stipulated that the first-level settlement should be collected before October of the 23rd year, and the second-level settlement should be collected before the end of December of the 23rd year. Also due to various reasons, the first-level settlement failed to arrive as scheduled, causing the second-level settlement to also fail to be completed on time. The Ministry of Finance has repeatedly ordered results to be submitted. As of now, the collected materials have reached more than 85 percent, but Xinjiang and Guangdong provinces have not yet submitted them. It is estimated that it can be completed before the end of June. (6th Special Telegram)

Ministry of Finance Reorganizes Fujian Tobacco and Alcohol Tax 51

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, based on the detailed report submitted by Shi Jianhan regarding the reorganization of tobacco and alcohol tax revenue in Fujian Province, stated that the province's tobacco and alcohol tax revenue has been too low for years, resulting in national losses of over 200,000 annually. Various branch bureaus and collection bureaus have accumulated malpractices over the years, with private commissions alone totaling at least four to five thousand yuan per month, resulting in direct national losses of five to eight hundred thousand annually. The Ministry of Finance believes that the proposed reorganization measures in the original report are not without merit and has instructed the Director of the Fujian Stamp Tax Bureau to assess the situation, promptly formulate reorganization measures, and actively remedy the situation. The collection of tobacco and alcohol taxes in all subordinate areas must uniformly comply with the regulations and issue various certificates issued by the Ministry, absolutely prohibiting the private production of receipts to prevent the erosion of tax revenue. The Bureau Director should conduct strict inspections at all times, and any subordinate collection staff who dare to disobey the regulations should be severely punished according to the law. The original report's mention of private commissions indicates that this type of malpractice violates laws and regulations. The Bureau Director, now that the reorganization is beginning, must thoroughly eliminate all previous accumulated malpractices. (6th dispatch)

Northwest Inspection Report 84

— Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya

Shaanxi's Construction Projects and Plans (Continued)

(B) In terms of transportation construction, the most noteworthy event is the opening of the Longhai Railway to Xi'an at the end of last year. Although the new Tongxi section has not yet had stations built and the roadbed is not yet consolidated, the business situation is flourishing, indicating that the development of the railway's future will be directly proportional to the extension of the route. According to the Ministry of Railways' plan for the western expansion of the railway, the plan is to temporarily take the repair to Baoji as the standard. The Western Baoji Engineering Bureau will be set up, while proceeding with the Xi'an to Weiyang section and the Wei River Bridge project, and starting surveying the Xianyang to Baoji route. Highways: (A) Highways under the Northwest Transportation Construction System of the Economic Commission, (1) Xi'an-Lanzhou Highway, over 750 kilometers long. The section within Shaanxi Province, from Xi'an via Xianyang, Liquan, Qianxian, Yongshou, Zhaoxian to Changwu, is 236 kilometers. This section was originally a provincial road, but was brought under the management of the Xi'an-Lanzhou Highway Bureau on the first day of this year. The entire road crosses mountains and ridges, and the project is arduous. In the Qing Dynasty, Zuo Zongtang once used soldiers to build a post road. In recent years, the China International Famine Relief Commission rebuilt it again to allow passage. Now the Economic Commission has spent hundreds of thousands of yuan to complete the so-called standard earthen road. It can be said that the construction has been costly. To facilitate commercial transportation on the entire road, it could have been barely opened to traffic last year. The Xi'an-Lanzhou Highway Bureau has now set the date of May 1 for a formal opening ceremony and has re-stipulated driving times and fares to facilitate commercial transportation and benefit traffic.

(2) Xi'an-Hanzhong Highway, from Xi'an via Xianyang, Wugong, Qishan, Baoji, Fengxian, Liuba, Baocheng, etc., to Nanzheng County, a total of 420 kilometers. The section from Xi'an to Fengxiang borrows the Xifeng section of the provincial road Xi'an-Longhai Road. The section from Fengxiang to Hanzhong is currently being built by the Economic Commission.

(B) Provincial roads under the Transportation Construction System of the Construction Department, (3) Xi'an-Tongguan Road, from Xi'an via Lintong, Weinan, Huayin to Tongguan, 167 kilometers long. Since the opening of the Longhai Railway to Xi'an, the freight costs have been low, causing the automobile business to gradually decline. There is also the "Xi'an-Tongguan North Branch Road," also known as the Xi'an-Chaoyi Road, which crosses the Wei River via Sanyuan, Fuping, Pucheng, Dali, and Chaoyi, with a total length of 260 kilometers. (4) Xi'an-Longxian Road, from Xi'an via Fengxiang and other places to Longxian, is 347 kilometers long. (Fengxiang's specialty sorghum wine is sold extensively in various places.) (5) Xi'an-Changwu and (6) Xi'an-Hanzhong roads have been taken over by the Economic Commission. (7) Xi'an-(missing character) Road, from Xi'an via Lantian, Shangxian, Shangnan, to Zijing Pass, is 403 kilometers long. However, the section from Lantian to Zijing Pass, which is 355 kilometers long, has no funding and has only been surveyed and has not yet been built. (8) Xianyang-Yulin Road, from Xianyang via Jingyang, Sanyuan, Yaoxian, Tongguan, Yijun, Central, Luochuan, (missing character)xian, Ganquan, Fushi, Yanchang, Yanchuan, Qingjian, Suide, Mizhi, to Yulin, is 829 kilometers long. The Xianyang to Sanyuan section is open to traffic. This spring, in promoting ethnic tomb-sweeping, it was further extended to the county where the Huangling Mausoleum is located, about 200 kilometers from Anxi. The entire road is planned to first repair the Sanyuan to Oil Field section, and each county has been ordered to first repair the earthen roads within their boundaries. Stone works, bridges, and culverts are currently being planned for repair. The above are the main trunk lines. The branch lines include roads from Xi'an to Sanyuan, to Ziwu Town, and to South Wutai, as well as from Sanyuan to Weinan, each several tens of kilometers long and already open to traffic. There is also a Han-Bai Road, from Nanzheng via Chenggu, Xixiang, Shiquan, Hanyin, Ankang, Xunyang to Baihe, 560 kilometers long. It has been roughly surveyed and completed, and if formally built, it will cost more than 2 million yuan. Currently, there is no capacity to do so. However, due to military relations, orders have been received to rush the construction of a temporary road.

In addition, the Construction Department is also preparing to establish the Xijing Electric Company. It was originally planned as a joint venture between the government and merchants, with a capital of 500,000 yuan. However, because it was difficult to raise merchant shares, it was changed to a completely government-run enterprise. The generator will temporarily purchase 750 kilowatts. The business scope is limited to electric lights, electricity, and electric heat. The Central Construction Committee has invested an old machine as a share, valued at a certain price. The factory site has now been selected outside the Xihuo Lane in the North Gate of Xi'an. According to Construction Director Lei Baohua, the preparations are planned to be completed before September of this year, capable of providing 30,000 electric lights. 38 counties in Guanzhong have already installed ring-type telephones, and two of them have even self-managed long-distance telephones. However, the long-distance telephone network should be handled by the Ministry of Communications, so other counties will no longer expand.

Yellow River security afforestation has also been strongly promoted recently. The Ministry of Industry plans to allocate 20,000 yuan from this year's budget to subsidize the three provinces of Shaanxi, Gansu, and Suiyuan. The three provinces will each raise 18,000 yuan to plant trees along the river as appropriate. The Shaanxi Construction Department has sent personnel to investigate the Yellow River embankment. According to the section north of Yumenkou, pine, cypress, Chinese toon, elm, and locust trees can be widely planted. Moreover, there are currently jujube, pear, mulberry, willow, and other fruit trees between the ditches and streams along the coast. Although they have not formed large-scale forests, they are scattered, growing in clumps. The types of trees that already exist can be used to fully plant along the river, so as to form an economic forest. The southern section, from Yumenkou to Wuliguan in Tongguan, is about 280 li long, not mountainous like the northern section, but entirely plains. The river water flows east and west, varying in width from one li to tens of li. Embankment afforestation in the northern section is like locking the stable door after the horse has bolted, as the riverside houses and fields in each county are almost level with the river surface. Every year in early spring, when the ice and snow melt upstream, or during heavy rains in July and August, the area immediately becomes a swamp, and lamentation echoes everywhere. Therefore, disaster prevention by afforestation in this section is particularly urgent.

Regarding the construction of the Xijing municipal government, it should have been handled by the Xijing City. However, Xijing City has not yet been established. In July of last year, the Xijing Preparatory Committee, the National Economic Commission, and the Construction Department, representing the Shaanxi Provincial Government, jointly formed a Xijing Municipal Construction Committee to take charge of municipal construction. The Xijing Preparatory Committee's expenses are 3,000 yuan per month (?). Since then, it has received 30,000 yuan in Xijing City expenses from the Ministry of Finance each month, which it transferred to the Municipal Construction Committee. The Municipal Construction Committee then decided on various municipal projects, which it forwarded to the Provincial Government for orders or directly to the Construction Department for execution. The required project funds were also directly delivered to the Construction Department for receipt. Overall, the work of the various agencies can be briefly described as repairing crushed stone roads within the city, opening railway station gates, measuring the city's water level, formulating urban road maps and charts, preserving historical sites, repairing mausoleums, ancient ancestral halls, and sidewalks, etc. As a result, the ancient Chang'an has gradually taken on a new look. However, it seems that the agencies are somewhat redundant and the authority is not fully centralized. This is perhaps an inevitable phenomenon during any reform and creation.

Japanese Army in Eastern Chahar Changes Village and Town Names 85

Using Names of Japanese Officers Participating in the Invasion of Chahar and Place Names to Commemorate Fallen Officers

Zhangjiakou Correspondent: The Japanese army recently attacked the border of Chahar Province, forcibly occupying Xiaochangzi, Shitouchengzi, Wunihe Weizi, Beishizhuzi, Changliang, Duanmuliang area, which belongs to Guyuan County. These areas were designated as the Fengning County area of ​​Rehe Province, adding a Sixth District, and setting up a pseudo-national border special inspection team administrative office. The names of the main villages and towns in the district were uniformly replaced with the names of non-commissioned officers in the Japanese army during the invasion of Chahar: 1. Nanweizi was renamed Guweizi (after the Japanese Gu Detachment Commander). 2. Xiaochang (Yongan Fort) was renamed Yongjian Fort (after the Japanese Yongjian Team Commander). 3. Shichengbao (Shitoucheng) was renamed Shijing Fort (after the Japanese Shijing Team Commander). 4. Changliang was renamed Lintian Fort (after the Japanese Lintian Team Commander). 5. Wunihe Weizi (Feicai Weizi) was renamed Songtian Fort (after the Japanese Songtian Team Commander). 6. Beishizhuzi was renamed Yan Zhong Fort (after the Japanese Yan Zhong Staff Officer). 7. Renhe Fort (Naobaohuai Weizi) was renamed Songjing Fort (after the Japanese Songjing Special Service Chief). The names of other small villages and towns remained the same. Some strategic locations were also renamed: 1. The high ground east of Duanmuliang was renamed Saito Mountain (in memory of the fallen Lieutenant Saito). 2. The high ground west of Duanmuliang was renamed Songtian Mountain (in memory of the fallen Team Commander Songtian). 3. The high ground north and south of Duanmuliang was renamed Jinli Mountain (in memory of the fallen Team Commander Jinli). 4. The middle of Duanmuliang was renamed Yongjian Liang (in memory of the fallen Team Commander Yongjian). (Northeast News Agency)

Jinan May Third Tragedy Commemoration 86

Meetings held simultaneously throughout Shandong Province

Jinan Correspondent: The May Third Tragedy occurred seven years ago. The people of Shandong, remembering that the blood of their compatriots had not yet dried and that the scars of the artillery fire had not yet healed, and reflecting on the pain, were overwhelmed with grief and indignation. They held a meeting in the Provincial Party Headquarters' auditorium at 9:00 AM this morning to express their continued remembrance. The entire province lowered flags to half-mast, suspended entertainment, and all schools took a day off. At the same time, people from all over held memorial meetings at the local Party headquarters to commemorate the seventh anniversary of the May Third Tragedy. Regarding the situation of the meeting in Jinan City, at 9:00 AM this morning, more than 1,000 representatives from all walks of life held a representative memorial meeting in the Provincial Party Headquarters' auditorium, presided over by Li Wenzhai. After opening the meeting, Li Wenzhai reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that the Jinan Tragedy occurred in 1928, and the people of the whole country were in grief and anger. It was truly a great humiliation to our country. Although seven years have passed, the national situation is still critical. All Chinese people should strive to become strong and share the responsibility of saving the country. Today, everyone is here to commemorate May Third. We must recognize the current situation of the country and strive to wash away this shame, so as not to betray the meaning of the memorial meeting, he said. This was followed by speeches by Qin Qirong, a member of the Provincial Executive Committee, and others, which were all extremely tragic. The meeting adjourned at around 11:00 AM. (3rd)

Reclaimed Areas of Southern Jiangxi Actively Reorganizing Land 87

—Providing Loans to Farmers to Resume Cultivation—

A dispatch from Fuchang: The Jiangxi Provincial Rural Cooperation Committee was previously ordered to handle rural relief in the bandit areas of southern Jiangxi. An appropriation of 700,000 yuan was made from the Post-War Rehabilitation Fund. The plan was to loan 100,000 yuan to disaster-stricken farmers in each of the six counties of Ningdu, Xingguo, Yudu, Hui’chang, Ruizhi, and Shicheng. The remaining 100,000 yuan was to be used for land management. Zou Huagai was appointed as the director of the Rural Relief and Land Management Office for the six counties, with an office established in Ningdu and branches in each county to actively carry out the work. According to a letter from Ningdu, the reclaimed areas here are desolate and miserable beyond description. However, the local products are abundant, the people are strong and brave, deeply resent the bandits, and eagerly hope for governance. It is expected that the old appearance can be restored in a few years. The offices in the six counties are proceeding according to the newly promulgated Rural Relief and Land Management Plan of the Headquarters. Regarding the abolition of land boundaries by the Red bandits, due to the utter chaos, they will be reorganized to determine ownership, rectify boundaries, and eliminate disputes, so that everyone has land to cultivate, and every field has someone to cultivate it. At the same time, disaster-stricken farmers who are unable to resume cultivation will first be organized into cooperative societies, and then provided with loans to purchase plowing cattle, seeds, farm tools, and food to resume cultivation and engage in production. Currently, one-third of each of these tasks has been completed. As of April 20th, there are 400 cooperative societies in the six counties, with more than 4,400,000 farmers participating. Loans of more than 100,000 yuan have been issued, and progress is continuing. (May 4th)

Headquarters Convenes Military Industry and Construction Conference 88

Experts from National Construction Agencies Attend / Proposals Reviewed by Four Groups / Conference Scheduled for Three Days

A dispatch from Hankou: Chairman Chiang, in order to promote the National Economic Construction Movement, has been actively advocating military industry and construction. Recently, he telegraphed the Headquarters to convene responsible personnel and experts from national construction agencies to hold a Military Industry and Construction Conference to study and implement the plan. The conference opened at 10:00 a.m. on the 3rd at the Headquarters. More than 70 representatives from provincial construction agencies and directors of various departments of the Headquarters, totaling more than 70 people, attended. Zhang Xueliang, Director of the Headquarters, had not yet returned to Hubei and was represented by Chief of Staff Qian Dajun as chairman. He also delivered a speech on behalf of Chairman Chiang, which stated: "Today, the Military Industry and Construction Conference opens. Chairman Chiang is in Guizhou supervising the remnants of bandits, and Director Zhang has also flown out on official business and are unable to attend. I will say a few words on behalf of the Chairman. Currently, the most important and urgent problems facing our country are nothing more than bandit suppression, national defense, and construction. In terms of importance, bandit suppression is of course the first priority, followed by national defense, and then construction. However, under the current international situation and the urgent needs of the national economy and the people's livelihood, it is necessary to plan for all three and advance them simultaneously. Therefore, during the period of implementing military bandit suppression, we must, of course, aim at bandit suppression while also taking into account the two conditions of national defense and construction. Conversely, when we carry out construction work, we should also strive to take into account the two conditions of national defense and bandit suppression. The significance of this Military Industry and Construction Conference lies in this, and the significance of our future implementation of military industry will also lie in this. In his speech at the welcoming meeting for the Yunnan and Guangxi armies in 1922, the Premier spoke of peaceful unification and transforming soldiers into workers. When we recall the Premier's raising of this issue at that time, it had a very profound and significant meaning. Because the army is only prepared but not used in peacetime, it can be said that it can only consume and cannot engage in production. In wartime, it is nothing more than fighting for cities and seizing land, it can be said that it is only destructive and cannot engage in construction. How can we transform these armies, which only consume and only destroy, into producers and builders that benefit the country and the people? I think that any country will feel the importance of this issue when disposing of surplus troops after the war. This Military Industry and Construction Conference should research and discuss this important point. Military industry and construction can be divided into two aspects. From the perspective of the military, it is how to transform all the troops into good soldiers, then transform the good soldiers into good citizens, and then transform the good citizens into good workers. From the perspective of construction, it is how to train and use these soldiers to do construction work, how to maximize the effectiveness of military workers, and how to engage in productive enterprises. At the same time, how can we ensure that the armed comrades who have survived hundreds of battles can find a career and security? These are all the main issues that need to be urgently studied and resolved at this Military Industry and Construction Conference. In other words, the Military Industry and Construction Conference can also be said to be proceeding with this meaning in mind. As for the standards for carrying out military industry and construction, first, it must be a work that requires more manpower and a longer time; second, it is a work that is easy for soldiers to do under the guidance of technical personnel and does not require a long period of training; and third, it is a work that can concentrate the troops in one place for easy command and management. Speaking of the methods of implementation, we are prepared to select one of the projects that have been planned and financed by the various construction agencies, which are prepared to solicit bids from merchants, and take them to be tried out by military industry. Once we have achieved results, we will actively promote them. Today, many of the comrades attending the meeting are construction experts and responsible personnel from national construction agencies. In terms of theory and experience, they naturally have a lot to contribute. I hope that they will give full play to their opinions on the military industry and construction plan, and study and discuss it in detail, so as to seek a bright future for the country, the nation, and the army from the three conditions of bandit suppression, national defense, and construction." On the morning of the 4th, the first general meeting was held at the Headquarters, still chaired by Qian Dajun. He reported on the 24 proposals from various parties and divided them into four groups for review: agriculture and forestry, general affairs, road administration, and water and soil conservation. Zhao Lianfang and others were designated as review committee members for the first group, Cai Guangxun and others for the second group, Liu Shoupeng and others for the third group, and Zhang Hanying and others for the fourth group. After the adjournment, the groups convened review meetings separately, preparing to submit them for discussion at the second general meeting on the 9th. The conference is scheduled for three days and will close immediately. (4th)

Zhejiang Province Promotes Cotton Industry Plan 89

—To be Carried Out in Three Years—

A dispatch from Quzhou: Most of the cotton produced in Zhejiang Province is of a coarse grade, which is not suitable for modern needs. Therefore, the Department of Construction has been making efforts to promote fine-grade cotton in recent years, and has made considerable progress. However, the planting area is too small and production is insufficient. Last year, the area of improved cotton fields promoted was only 20,000 mu, producing only 4,000 dan of cotton, which is not enough to meet the demand of domestic yarn factories. In order to develop cotton production and promote the improvement of coarse-grade cotton, the Department of Construction has decided to promote the improvement of 150,000 mu of cotton fields starting this year. 80,000 mu of Million Dollar cotton will be promoted in the cotton areas along the river in Hangzhou, Xiaoshan, Yuyao, Shaoxing, and Shangyu counties, and 70,000 mu of American cotton will be promoted in the coastal cotton areas of Zhenhai, Cixi, Yuyao, and Haiyan. This is because American cotton is suitable for the coast, and the soil properties for planting Million Dollar cotton are suitable for the riverbank. These cotton varieties have also been tested in Zhejiang Province for six or seven years, and the soil quality and climate are very suitable. Moreover, the quality is good enough to spin fine yarn of 20 counts or more, which can compete with fine-grade cotton from foreign countries. The yield is higher than that of local varieties, and the value is 20% higher. The Agricultural Management Committee estimates that the yield of improved cotton is 80 catties of cotton seeds per mu, which is calculated to be 24 catties of lint cotton per mu, about one dan of lint cotton per four mu. 150,000 mu can produce 30,000 dan of cotton, and the income can be increased to 1.5 million yuan. As for the promotion methods, a three-year plan will be implemented. In the first year, 150,000 mu of improved cotton fields will be promoted, producing 30,000 dan of cotton, and the income will be 1.5 million yuan. In the second year, 500,000 mu of improved cotton fields will be promoted, producing 120,000 dan of cotton, and the income can be increased to 6 million yuan. In the third year, 1 million mu of improved cotton fields will be promoted, producing 500,000 dan of cotton, and the income can be increased to 25 million yuan. Half of the promoted cotton fields will be improved from local cotton fields, and half will be reclaimed from wasteland. A certain amount of local cotton fields will still be retained to meet the needs for planting coarse-grade cotton. (4th)

Songjiang Police Chief's Dereliction of Duty Debate Concludes 90

Li Zehuan (from Hunan), the chief of the First Branch of the Songjiang County Public Security Bureau (stationed in Tinglin Town), released morphine offenders Sun X, Chen X, and Zhang X, along with six small packets of morphine, after the Hougang police station apprehended them. After the case was transferred to the bureau, Dai X provided bail and they were released, causing a public outcry and allegations of bribery. After the Third District Party Department discovered this, Li immediately fled to Suzhou with his family and was apprehended by Fei Gongxia of the Water Patrol Team and sent to the court's prosecutor's office for investigation. On the morning of the sixth, Judge Zhang Yihuang summoned Hougang patrolman Xiao Huanjun, First Branch guard Xu Faren, clerk Tao Huimin, and Hua Yutong, Chen Quqing, and others to court to examine the case. Prosecutor Liu presented his arguments in court. Patrolman Xiao testified about the circumstances of the arrest. Guard Xu testified that the chief made the decision to release them and that he did not know the details of the bribery. Clerk Tao testified that the bail bond was written by him at the chief's order, that the guarantor was surnamed Dai, that he did not remember the name, and that he did not know anything else. Hua Yutong and Chen Quqing both testified that they were not involved in the case and that the rumors of a three- or four-hundred-yuan bribe were just street talk and not credible. Chief Li was brought to court and claimed that Hua and Chen had come to him and that the bail bond was written with the surname Dai. He said that the case file had been lost, so he did not remember the name. He also claimed that the Sun and Shen were opium smokers, not morphine users, that the small packets contained coffee sugar instead of morphine, and that he did not receive any bribes. The judge announced the conclusion of the debate and that the verdict would be announced on the tenth. Li and Tao were returned to custody, and the others were dismissed.

Campaign for Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Drafting Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law 93

The Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Campaign Committee organized by the National Lawyers Association convened a general meeting in Suzhou on the 5th. More than 20 representatives from various places attended. The details have been briefly recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now reported that the meeting lasted for five hours and decided to draft the principles of the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Law, including: (1) the scope of claims for damages; (2) the scope of claims for damages that are not allowed; (3) the subject of claims for damages; (4) the period for claims for damages; (5) the right to withdraw claims for damages; (6) the statute of limitations for exercising the right to claim damages; (7) the right to entrust an agent to claim damages; (8) the method of compensation for damages; (9) the method of application and the court with jurisdiction. The deadline is ten days for each committee member to submit written opinions for the drafting committee to adopt. After the drafting is completed, it will be submitted to the review committee for review. Shen Junru, Dai Tianqiu, Chen Dexin, Chen Yaodong, Wu Zengshan, Li Shirui, and Huang Weishi were immediately elected as the seven members of the review committee. The meeting place is still the Wu County Lawyers Association, and letters will be sent to lawyers associations in various places to investigate the actual materials of wrongful imprisonment for reference.

Wuxi's Hou Zhai Bandit Alarm Villagers Capture Thieves 94

Zhang Jingtang, a villager from Huajiaqiao near Wangting Township in the Houzhai area of the Eighth District, originally from Jiangyin, usually rows a boat in the Hengfeng Sauce Garden in Shanghai. He recently happened to be at home. At one o'clock the night before, the family had already gone to sleep when four bandits suddenly broke into the house, tied up the family members, both male and female, and looted everything. They stole all the rice, clothes, and money and loaded them onto the boat docked on the riverbank. Just as they were about to escape, they were discovered by neighbors, who immediately beat gongs and gathered to pursue them. The bandits hurriedly rowed the boat to the opposite bank, but they had already alarmed Zou Xinzhuo, the head of Beidu Township, and more than ten villagers, including Yang Errong, Hua Guilin, and Hua Xinggen, who divided up and surrounded them. Seeing that there were many people surrounding them, the bandits abandoned their loot and landed, hiding in the wheat fields. When Zou and others chased them, they saw that the boat was empty and the bandits had fled. They searched everywhere until the next morning when they captured the four bandits, Xue Keming, Ma Futang, Gu Jiaquan, and Zhao Linchang, in the wheat fields. They were immediately taken to the office of the security regiment. Under interrogation, they confessed that they had been involved in robberies in Wuxian County. They immediately telegraphed the County Public Security Bureau, which sent investigator Luo Shaoxiang and others to the township to escort the four bandits to the city. A steel bar, a fake Mauser pistol, and many stolen items of clothing were found in the bandit boat. The case has been reported to Director X for investigation, and the bandit boat has been handed over to the village head for safekeeping.

Adding Railroad Tracks and Installing Long-Distance Telephones 97

In order to facilitate the operation of railroad vehicles throughout the country, the Ministry of Railways immediately ordered Lu Weiyan, the chief of the Changzhou-Danyang-Suzhou section of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, to order the stationmasters of each station to actively plan and rectify. After receiving the order, Li Guisheng, the stationmaster of Wuxi Station, argued that Wuxi Station had more vehicles than other stations, and that the loading and unloading of goods by merchants was also not small. Therefore, he proposed to add a track of about five or six zhang from Yangqi in Dongli to the original Yangqi in the west of Fenlu. The roadbed has already been built. The Railway Administration ordered the Shanghai Engineering Department to be responsible for the preparations. Twenty new-style telephones have been prepared and will be installed first in Shanghai and Changzhou stations. Wuxi Station will also need to install them soon. The original telegraph machines will not be changed and will continue to send messages as usual.

Yangzhou's Yangjing Road Shahe Dam Washed Away by Water 98

The construction of the Yangjing Road, the north-south section of the Shahe River in the fourth district of this county, was ordered to be completed within a limited time. Construction usually starts in July. So far, the Shahe Dam has been completed eighty or ninety percent. Unexpectedly, now, during the time of a surge of tides, a corner of the completed project was washed away. They are currently rushing to build a sleeve filling, but the dam extends for thirty-eight continents and the water flow is very rapid. With three tides a day, if there is a major flood before the culvert is built, the filled dam will also be washed away to the east. It is reported that the Bureau of Construction has informed the Road Engineering Office of this situation, requesting that the culvert be built quickly to avoid further damage to the road construction.

Zhenjiang Checks Salt Used by Soy Sauce Shops 101

Soy sauce shops in Zhenjiang have always gone to official salt depots to collect Zhejiang salt. Each soy sauce vat is required to collect 850 catties of salt per year according to regulations. In recent years, some shops have collected more salt than they should, while others have collected less. Song Zian, the deputy salt commissioner of Songjiang, specially commissioned Ling Xichao, the district chief of the Sixth District of the Tax Police, and Liu Shengqi, the section chief of the Songjiang Audit Office, and Bao X of the road section, to come to Zhenjiang to check the number of vats door-to-door, make a list, and have the checked soy sauce shops stamp the list with their shop seals, and check whether they are mixing refined salt and other types of salt to make soy sauce. Ling and the other two arrived in Zhenjiang yesterday and first checked the area around the small dock. Today they will check the various townships and towns in the city and will also go to check them.

Yesterday's British Emperor's Ascension Anniversary Celebration British Community Celebrates Enthusiastically 107

Over a Thousand People Attend Morning Prayer / Evening Parade and Torch Display

Yesterday was the 25th anniversary of the ascension of British Emperor George V. The British officials and merchants in Shanghai celebrated enthusiastically. A prayer ceremony was held in the morning, and a carnival was held in the afternoon. The British troops stationed in Shanghai also held a parade at the Racecourse last night and displayed torches, which was quite lively. Details of the various events are described below:

Celebration Prayer Yesterday at 10:00 a.m., a celebration prayer service was held in the Grand Hall on Jiangxi Road. After the old pastor led the ceremony as usual, (illegible) retreated to the lawn in front of the hall, where the British community sang the British national anthem. The ceremony ended at around 11:00 a.m. and photographs were taken. In addition to British Consul General in Shanghai, Brenan, and the entire British community in Shanghai, those who attended included Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director Yu Ming of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, and Consul General of the United States Kenningham, Consul General of France Badas, Consul General of Japan Ishisa, and military officers of various countries stationed in Shanghai, totaling over a thousand people.

At the same time, various British schools held dances and performances of songs.

Torch Display At 9:00 p.m. last night, the British Navy and Army held a parade at the Racecourse and invited officers from various countries to attend. The lights in the Racecourse were as bright as day. The program included: (1) firing 21 cannons; (2) changing the old and new parade styles; (3) a performance by 300 sailors and two land cannons; (4) a performance of the changes in military uniforms from 1689, 1740, 1760, 1815, 1830, and 1900; (5) military music; (6) a human pyramid formed by 48 British Boy Scouts; (7) an electric light display; (8) high jump; (9) torches; (10) (illegible)

Small Credit Loans: Changes in the Distribution of Amounts 108

Banks Confirm 1.5 Million, Money Shops Also Decide on 1 Million

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the 5 million yuan loan for the relief of industry and commerce jointly organized by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, as well as the banking and money shop associations, since Minister of Finance Kong invited financial circles to a tea party a few days ago to exchange opinions and urge its implementation, the amounts undertaken by each party have been changed. The Banking Association held a special meeting yesterday to discuss it, and the Money Shop Association will also hold a meeting in the coming days to discuss and formally implement it. The timeline for this should not be far off. The details are as follows:

Redistribution of Confirmed Amounts: Regarding the 5 million yuan loan for the relief of industry and commerce jointly organized by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, as well as the banking and money shop associations, after receiving the instructions and ten principles from the Ministry of Finance, it has not been implemented due to the ongoing discussions on the loan amounts undertaken by each party. Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi specifically invited representatives from Shanghai's financial circles to a tea party at his residence last Saturday. Responsible persons from the banking and money shop associations, such as Ye Fu, Qin Runqing, etc., attended. After exchanging opinions, it was decided that the Central Bank and Bank of China would each commit 1 million yuan, and the Bank of Communications would commit 500,000 yuan, totaling 2.5 million yuan for the three banks. In addition, the Banking Association would commit 1.5 million yuan, and the Money Shop Association would commit 1 million yuan.

Suspension of the Subcommittee: The Banking Association previously, in response to the requests of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Local Association, and Shanghai's industrial and commercial circles, handled credit loans. A subcommittee was established, and member banks were notified to confirm the loan amounts undertaken. The Bank of China committed 1 million yuan, the Bank of Communications committed 400,000 yuan, and other banks committed 475,000 yuan, totaling 1,875,000 yuan. However, after Minister Kong convened a meeting with banking circles and decided to expand the program, the subcommittee suspended its activities to participate in the larger initiative. It was originally intended to incorporate the amounts already committed by each bank, and a meeting was convened to decide to send Ye Fu and Wang Yansong, two standing committee members, as representatives. The result of Minister Kong's subsequent convening of a meeting to distribute the amounts has resulted in changes. Since the 1.4 million yuan already committed by the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will be put forward, the association convened another meeting yesterday to discuss the distribution of amounts among the banks.

Resolution of the Banking Association Yesterday: The Banking Association specifically convened its 67th Executive Committee meeting at 1:30 PM yesterday, and invited all member banks to attend. Executive Committee members Ye Fu, Wang Yansong, Xu Jiqing, Wang Zhixin, Qu Jigang, etc., and representatives from all member banks, totaling more than 30 people, attended. Ye Fu was unanimously elected as chairman. After the formalities, Ye Fuxiao first reported on the proceedings of the tea party attended by Minister Kong and the revised distribution of amounts. Of the amount already committed by the Banking Association, excluding the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, only 475,000 yuan was available. It was resolved on how to raise the remaining 1.5 million yuan: (1) Each member bank of the Banking Association will commit 1 million yuan, and those that have already committed will be notified to double their commitment. (2) Banks that have not committed or have committed a smaller amount will be requested to commit or increase their commitment. (3) For the remaining 500,000 yuan, the Ministry of Finance will be requested to negotiate with non-member banks to commit. (4) Ye Fuxiao and Wang Yansong, two standing committee members, will be appointed to report to the Minister of Finance. Next, Secretary-General Lin Kanghou reported on the recent negotiations regarding the Post Office's restriction on attaching letters to remittances. It was resolved to notify all member banks: (1) to comply with the Postal Regulations, and (2) to use remittance slips instead of attached letters to the greatest extent possible. The meeting adjourned around 2:00 PM.

Money Shops Will Also Hold Meetings to Discuss: As for the money shops, the previous meeting of member representatives resolved to agree to participate and decided that each member money shop would commit an equal share, totaling 250,000 yuan. Minister Kong's tea party requested an increase to 1 million yuan. The association will also convene a meeting to report and discuss ways to increase the commitment. However, the meeting date has not yet been decided. It is heard that after substantial contact is made regarding the distribution of amounts by each party, a meeting will be scheduled to discuss implementation. When formally implemented, a committee will be formed according to the provisions of Articles 9 and 10 of the principles promulgated by the Ministry of Finance to preside over it. The Ministry of Finance may also appoint representatives to participate.

Special Rights Clauses for the International Exchange Bank 109

The Ministry of Finance Will Soon Announce

According to a Central News Agency report from Nanjing on the 6th, the Ministry of Finance will announce the special rights clauses granted to the International Exchange Bank as follows: (1) The assets, deposits, or other funds of the International Exchange Bank, whether in times of peace or war, shall not be subject to any restrictions, such as inspection or confiscation, and shall not be subject to restrictions on the export of gold or foreign currency or other similar interference. (2) If disputes arise between the Chinese government and the International Exchange Bank for the purpose of implementing Article 1, the dispute shall be submitted to an arbitration tribunal. Each party must appoint a member to the arbitration tribunal. If the two arbitrators cannot agree on the selection of a presiding judge, the person proposed by the President of the International Court of Justice at The Hague shall be the presiding judge.

National Federation of Commerce Plans to Establish a Commercial Joint Bank, with Each Store Contributing Five Yuan 111

Mr. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, previously received a letter from the Guangdong Chamber of Commerce advocating that the National Federation of Commerce initiate the organization of a Commercial Joint Bank to concentrate strength and circulate finance. Mr. Lin then sent letters to chambers of commerce across the country to solicit opinions. He has now received replies of support from the chambers of commerce in Hubei and other provinces. Mr. Lin is drafting organizational laws and plans for raising shares. The motivation and implementation methods of the initiative are as follows:

Motivation: According to the person in charge of the federation, in recent years, China's economy has been declining, and commerce has been sluggish. Although the reasons are multifaceted, they are mainly due to the invasion of foreign goods and the collapse of the rural economy. Exhaustion has not occurred overnight. Recently, the global economic downturn and the impact of silver policies have further dealt a major blow. At this critical time for the survival of the commercial economy, there is no way to reverse the decline without uniting in spirit and concentrating strength. Therefore, it is proposed to unite the chambers of commerce of various provinces and cities across the country in order to establish the most powerful financial institution and devote itself to the relief of commerce and the rural economy.

Implementation Methods: The implementation method is to require each member store of the local chambers of commerce to subscribe for a minimum of five yuan as a necessary condition. With the large number of chambers of commerce and member stores across the country, it is enough to accumulate little by little to easily establish a Commercial Joint Bank with strong capital. Moreover, this method is most suitable for modern commercial economic principles. China has a vast territory, and transportation is inconvenient. In addition to the major cities, there are many places where the remittance network is not accessible, so the economy cannot be active and commerce cannot develop. If the Commercial Joint Bank is established, then wherever there is a chamber of commerce in the country, that is where the economic power reaches. Even in remote areas, ways can be found to circulate finance, and this can be used to unify the connections of merchants, which will greatly benefit the future of commerce and the adjustment of the rural economy. Everything is interconnected.

Joint Office Operation by the Municipal Government: Still Difficult in Practice 114

According to the Central News Agency, in order to simplify operations, the Municipal Government plans to implement a joint office system. Mayor Wu has instructed the Secretariat to draft measures. According to a responsible person of the Municipal Government, some provinces have already implemented joint office operation. In addition to supervising subordinate agencies, it also performs executive functions. Therefore, joint office operation is still difficult in practice. The current plan is to first eliminate redundant agencies to save public funds, while striving for simplicity in operations. Lawyers Association: Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement 115

The Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Lawyers Association of the Republic of China issued a declaration yesterday stating: "In accordance with the resolution of the Sixth Congress of Representatives, the Association has organized the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee to seek the realization of a national compensation system. From the beginning of the movement, public opinion has been greatly in favor. Now, at the plenary committee meeting held in Suzhou, after detailed discussion, it is believed that the legal community nationwide should concentrate its efforts and proceed in unison to meet the requirements of social justice and promote the country's fulfillment of its moral and legal obligations. Considering modern civilized countries, since the end of the 19th century, with the changes of the times and the advancement of the theory of corporate responsibility, in terms of public and private law, it is common practice to provide compensation to the people for damages caused by the exercise of power by government agencies. The wrongful imprisonment compensation system is also based on the two kinds of responsibilities of the state in public and private law. The legislative examples include those that have enacted special laws, such as Germany and Austria, those that have stipulated it in the Criminal Procedure Law, such as France and Italy, and those that have established it as a precedent, such as England and the United States. Although the forms vary, it is always the same that the state should be responsible for compensating innocent citizens for improper damages caused by the exercise of power by its judicial organs, whether due to the pure official actions of judicial officials or the illegal actions of judicial officials taking advantage of their positions. Looking back at our country, the wrongful imprisonment compensation system, after the Qin and Han Dynasties, ultimately could not eliminate wrongful imprisonments, so it severely punished those who caused them, based on the principle of retribution. Emperor Gaozong of the Song Dynasty provided money and rice to those who were innocently released to return home, reducing the material losses suffered by the innocent due to the improper actions of state organs. However, the idea of state compensation was not established as a regular law. The Ming Law had provisions for the perpetrator to compensate the victim's property. However, for wrongful imprisonments caused by judicial misconduct, the state was never held responsible for compensation. This kind of legislative example, which expresses autocratic thought, continued from the Qing Dynasty to the Republic of China without any change. Recently, the judicial system has not yet reached perfection, and although there are many judicial officials who are respected for their integrity, incorruptibility, law-abidingness, and impartiality, there are also many who are immoral, greedy for wealth, or have shallow knowledge and make hasty judgments. As a result, innocent people are wrongly accused, and their cries go unheard. How many of our people have been ruined and killed because of this! How many have been demoralized and unable to recover! A stroke of the pen in the courtroom, a thousand drops of blood below. This kind of tragic phenomenon still exists in 20th century China. What is the misfortune of the people like? The Association, mindful of the teachings of the weakness of the law and deeply concerned about the resentment of the courts, takes advantage of the opportunity of the chief judicial officer to rectify the system and discipline the officials, and is determined to realize the wrongful imprisonment compensation system to protect the right to life of our people and to improve the organization of our country. A country is an organic whole. If its constituent elements cannot pursue their legitimate survival, it is no different from the cells of the human body losing their physiological nutrition. If the cells do not receive nourishment, the person is injured. If the constituent elements are not protected in their survival, the country will not be a country. Therefore, the Association advocates that the state should compensate for wrongful imprisonments not only for the individual, but also to protect individuals for the sake of the country, and to protect its constituent elements. In other words, the Association's advocacy of wrongful imprisonment compensation is not subject to the legal thought of individualistic tendencies, but is subject to the legal thought of socialistic tendencies. This is especially what the Association must solemnly tell the people of our country. People of the country, would you like to sympathize with this movement of the Association and help it to be realized quickly? The Association is willing to work together with you to achieve it."

Last Day of Literacy Promotion Week: Today is Farmers' Promotion Day 118

Municipal Farmers' Association Issues a Letter to All Farmers in the City, Farmers' Associations in Various Districts Conduct Recreational Promotions Separately, Literacy School Teachers to Take Exams on the 10th

Today is the last day of the Literacy Movement Promotion Week in the city, which is Farmers' Promotion Day. The Municipal Farmers' Association leads farmers' associations in various districts to organize promotion teams and hold recreational gatherings. The Municipal Farmers' Association also issues a letter to all farmers in the city, detailing the various situations as follows:

Academic Promotion: Yesterday was Academic Promotion Day. All schools in the city, in addition to the principals of each school reporting on the meaning of literacy education during Memorial Week, also organized promotion teams of students to promote to the public in busy areas and distributed literacy promotion pictures and leaflets on the spot.

Teacher Examination Date: The deadline for registration for the association's recruitment of literacy school teachers was yesterday. A total of more than 900 people registered. The oral exam is scheduled for the 10th of this month and the written exam on the 11th. The location is Aurora University on Rue Labbé. An examination committee has been organized to preside over the exams.

Letter to the Educational Community: The Municipal Education Association issued a letter to colleagues in the educational community yesterday as follows: "We should all know that the current stage of the Chinese National Revolution is the "Construction Period", and the literacy education movement is the core of the construction work. Because China has more than 80% illiteracy and 10% semi-illiteracy (that is, although they know how to read, they lack common sense and civic training), it is undoubtedly lacking in theoretical basis and too far from the facts to ask them to shoulder the mission of building the country and benefiting society. Since the establishment of the first session of the Association, it has first noticed this most basic literacy education, created a one-yuan-a-month education movement, established many public schools, and educated thousands of illiterate people, and is still continuing to do so. However, we regret that we do not have many people and have limited ability. The one-yuan-a-month education movement has only achieved a very small effect on our ideals. Fortunately, the Municipal Government has launched a large-scale literacy education movement, aiming to eliminate illiteracy in the city within a year and make them all healthy citizens. This is the revolutionary process of the planning period, and this is a pioneering initiative of the literacy movement that has never been done before. On the occasion of the Academic Promotion Literacy Education Movement Day, the colleagues of the Association extend the following four hopes to the comrades in the educational community throughout the city: (1) Starting from today, every student should teach at least one illiterate person to read, for a period of two months, and then continue to teach. Teachers and staff in schools should gather them for training from time to time, and instill a lot of civic common sense. (2) Students in secondary schools and above should set up more public schools to provide literacy education, common sense guidance, and civic training. (3) School authorities should fully provide convenience for promoting the literacy education movement, both materially and spiritually. (4) School janitors, guards, and other workers in the school should first be encouraged to become literate in order to advocate for it. The above four points are the minimum duties that colleagues in the educational community should fulfill in promoting the literacy education movement. Because we can read and have knowledge and enjoy a unique cultural life, how can we not be served by a large group of hardworking people in society? In order to repay their kindness and fulfill our national duty, we must quickly get up and work hard to promote the literacy education movement."

Farmers' Promotion: Today is Farmers' Promotion Day. The South Shanghai District Farmers' Association and the Gaohang District Association held a recreational promotion meeting for literacy. The South Shanghai District's program included a drama by the New Farmers' Theater, a costumed speech by the Juvenile Speech Group, and magic. The Gaohang District's program included harmonica by the China Harmonica Association, Chinese martial arts by the Chinese Martial Arts Research Society, and a drama by Peiying Primary School. Farmers' associations in other districts organized promotion teams to go to the countryside to promote literacy. At the same time, literacy promotion was held during the Spring Plowing Movement Conference held in Yangsi District today. The Municipal Farmers' Association also plans to convene a discussion meeting with the cadres of farmers' associations in various districts to discuss the establishment of literacy schools in various districts.

Letter to Farmers: The Municipal Farmers' Association issued a letter to all farmers in the city as follows: "Dear farmers, do you know how many illiterate people there are in China? Can you imagine how painful those illiterate people are? Can you also imagine that because there are too many illiterate people in China, the country is weak and the people are poor? According to surveys and statistics, in every hundred Chinese people, about eighty are illiterate. Farmers account for a large part of these many illiterate people. If we compare this situation with foreign countries, it is naturally very different. Because in today's world, there is no country like China with so many illiterate people. In various parts of Japan, even rickshaw drivers and farmers can read and like to read the daily newspaper, so they can be strong. How painful it is for a person not to be literate! They cannot write, they cannot calculate, and they will not know ordinary common sense. How can they understand domestic politics and the international situation? Even their own farming affairs, such as new knowledge and new technologies, cannot be known or improved. Why? Because these all require the power of writing to be known. Not knowing how to read is painful. Dear farmers, it is really painful not to be literate, like a blind man with open eyes. If farmers do not know how to read, they will not be able to obtain all kinds of new agricultural knowledge, and agriculture will never progress. Now about 80% of the people in China are illiterate, so the lack of progress in all undertakings in China is inevitable. Therefore, it is an urgent matter to make many of our compatriots literate. Now the city's literacy movement is being actively launched. This is good news for our illiterate compatriots, and it is also the good news for our farmers, who account for the largest number of illiterate people. We demand the knowledge of writing, we demand the knowledge of all kinds of common sense needed in our lives, and we demand that we can be good citizens. Therefore, we should enthusiastically promote this great literacy movement. In the near future, dozens of schools will be established in various districts of the city. At that time, everyone who is illiterate will have to go to these schools to learn to read, reading for one hour a day. Tuition is free and books are given away. After graduating in two months, they will be able to keep accounts, write letters, and read simple newspapers. How convenient! If they really cannot go to school to study, then teachers will come to their homes to teach them in person. And after two months, if they pass the exam, they can also graduate. It is hoped that the dear farmers will unite to participate in this movement. It is hoped that the illiterate farmers will quickly go to literacy schools to study. This is not only to increase the daily knowledge and life of the illiterate farmers, but also a major key to reviving the countryside and improving the national status. Farmers, unite!"

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables Southwest Political Committee Requesting Suspension of National Special Tax on Domestic Agricultural Products 126

How can we divide ourselves within the same country, and there should be no more existence of distorted tax systems.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Southwest Political Affairs Committee in Guangzhou, the Guangdong Provincial Government, the Guangdong Department of Finance, and the Guangdong Provincial Party Headquarters (titles omitted). According to a letter from the Miscellaneous Grains and Oilseed Cake Industry Association on the 4th of this month, based on a letter from the Lyu Lan Business Miscellaneous Grain Help Shenshou Hall on April 26th, and a letter from the Guangzhou Peanut Sesame Miscellaneous Grain Industry Association, the Guangdong Department of Finance has been collecting taxes on peanuts, sesame, and other oilseeds at a rate of $1.80 per load for various beans and peanut kernels, $1.50 per load for shelled peanuts, and $3.50 per load for peanut oil and soybean oil, effective April 21st, which is unbearable for merchants. They requested an appeal. An examination of the special tax bureau for imported agricultural products and miscellaneous items established in Guangzhou in 1933 showed that regulations stipulated that domestic products were tax-exempt. Peanuts and oil transported to Guangdong come from Shandong, Henan, Hebei, Jiangsu, and other provinces and are purely domestic products, not imported goods. Not long after, the Guangdong authorities started collecting taxes in the name of “educating the countryside.” Now, taxes have been reimposed, which not only benefits imported products but also, during this period of commercial decline and economic hardship, how can businesses bear this heavy burden? This also greatly affects the domestic sale of agricultural products. Therefore, we earnestly request your association to telegraph the Guangdong Southwest Political Affairs Committee, the Provincial Government, the Department of Finance, and the Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters to consider the difficulties of merchants and the livelihood of the people and immediately abolish this tax. We also request that you appeal to the city chamber of commerce to show public spirit. According to this, the Guangdong province has been collecting special taxes on imported agricultural products for years, and domestic products are tax-exempt. Not for a year, it suddenly taxed domestic agricultural products in the name of saving the countryside. Now, it also heavily taxes peanut oil and beans transported from Yilu, Yu, and Su provinces to Guangdong. The policies have been inconsistent over the past two years, leaving farmers and merchants unable to bear the burden. In addition to telegraphed the Guangdong Provincial authorities to abolish it, we must also prepare letters to inform you, hoping that you will investigate and grant a unified appeal to enrich public morality and other matters. An investigation of the Guangdong Provincial Agricultural Special Tax Bureau shows that when it was first established, it was limited to imported goods, and it should not have changed its purpose to tax domestic goods. If it is to save the countryside, then Guangdong province is within the Chinese territory, and the bankruptcy of rural areas is a common phenomenon in all provinces. Why create divisions and harm one to benefit the other? Now that the transit taxes in various places are about to be abolished on a regular basis, within the same country, there should be no more existence of distorted systems of domestic passage tax. Guangdong province is setting an example of reforming various policies for the country and should not repeat this bad policy to be criticized. If other provinces also use saving their own agricultural products as an excuse to heavily tax the import of Guangdong's special products, how can Guangdong remain silent? The principle of loyalty and forgiveness is a good plan for collecting taxes and a key to national development. Our association is concerned about the interests of the Shanghai business community and the collection of taxes and dare not fail to do our best. We hope you will consider the situation and grant us the authority to suspend the tax for public convenience. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce,

Hangzhou Guanghua Match Factory Formally Merged into Dachanghua and Has Applied to the Ministry of Industry for Change of Registration 131

According to the Guomin News Agency, the Hangzhou Guanghua Match Factory, founded solely by Zhejiang gentry Tang Shouqian, was the first self-made match factory in China. Since its establishment, it has been a giant in the Chinese match industry for decades and the largest producer in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui unified tax area. The factory currently has more than 400 male workers and 700 female workers, totaling more than 1,000 people, and the scale can be imagined. Last year, match production was 32,643.6 cases, and the production volume in the previous year was 43,507.7 cases. Compared to each other, last year's production volume has been greatly reduced.

Formally merged in The factory has been experiencing difficulty in recent years due to competition from peers, resulting in a backlog of products and difficulty in selling them. Prices have also fallen tragically, making it difficult to maintain operations. Furthermore, increased unified taxes have made business even more difficult. Therefore, in July of last year, it joined Dachanghua Match Co., Ltd. Now, it has formally merged into Dachanghua Match Company and has submitted documents for change of registration and trademark transfer to the Ministry of Industry for registration.

Strong influence Investigation shows that Dachanghua Match Co., Ltd. was formed in July 1930 by merging three factories: Shanghai Yingchang Match Factory, Suzhou Hongsheng Factory, and Zhoupu Zhongping Factory. In December of the same year, it bid to buy the former Hankou Xiechang Factory and renamed it Gange YanChang. In July 1931, Jiujiang Yusheng Company also joined. In September of the same year, it set up a stem film factory in Donggou, Pudong. Now, the Hangzhou Guanghua Factory has also joined, and its influence is historically strong. The current general manager is Mr. Liu Hongsheng.

Westerners and Others Privately Manufacturing Narcotics Punished 135

A Westerner, Hagens, residing at No. 17 Fuen Road in the French Concession, previously reported to the Jing'an Temple police station by telephone, saying that his hired domestic servant, Wu Ruqing from Hebei, was suspected of colluding with others to privately manufacture the narcotic morphine. He requested an investigation. The Chinese detective Shi Sijian went to investigate and arrested Wu first. He was then taken to the morphine factory at No. 12 Pushi Road, where Pan Zhenlin, Liu Zhongxian, Zhao Jianqiu, Li Deyuan, Zhao Wu's wife, and others were apprehended. The manufacturing equipment and chemicals were also seized. They were all sent to the First Special Court. After several interrogations, the defendants jointly retained lawyers Fan Gang and Wu Linkun to defend them. The case has been interrogated and the final statements have been heard. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Zhaoxin presided over the eighth court to announce the judgment. The main text said: Zhao Jianqiu manufactured a substitute for opium and was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Wu Ruqing, Pan Zhenlin, and Liu Zhongxian helped in the manufacturing and were each sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Li Deyuan was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for the same crime. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined to be deducted at the rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Zhao Wu's wife was found not guilty. The confiscated contraband and objects used in the crime were confiscated according to the list.

Page 10

This Year's Fishing Season Peaceful on the Ocean Surface 136

However, the market price is falling, and the profits are much lower.

According to reports from various patrol ships of the Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry, this year's fishing season in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has been exceptionally peaceful. A total of five patrol ships have been dispatched to the fishing areas of Shengshan, Xiangshan, Shimen, Zhenhai, Ningbo Port, Dinghai, Huawu, and Shenjiamen. Due to the strict patrols, pirates have disappeared, and the ocean surface is peaceful. However, this year the price of small yellow croaker has fallen. At the end of April, the selling price per load was 60 cents to 1 yuan, and at most, it did not exceed 2 yuan. Many fishermen, believing that the price was too low, pickled salted goods and transported them to various places for sale. Therefore, the profits of fishermen this year are much lower than in previous years. The reason for the low price is that the discovery of fish schools was too late, which did not meet the timeliness. The Central News Agency reporter also inquired in detail with the person in charge of the Jiangzhe Cuttlefish Trap-netting dispute, which has been pending for years. According to reports, fishermen in Zhejiang Province all use trap-netting, while fishermen in Jiangsu Province use nets. If it is based on hindering reproduction, then the harm is equal. However, when trap-netting, the fish spawn in the traps. Because the walls of the traps are too dense, the eggs stick to the four sides of the traps. When they are taken out of the water, they are exposed to air, which causes the eggs to become infertile, causing more damage. When net-fishing, the eggs spawn in the nets, and the eggs are scattered in the sea and can survive. If they stick to the edges of the nets and are taken out of the water, the eggs will also be infertile, and the damage is less. However, according to Zhejiang Province fishermen, the windlass on the edges of the nets shakes and rotates on the seabed, which can also crush fish eggs, which is the same as trap-netting. This is the focus of the dispute. In short, trap-netting and net-fishing both have the harm of reducing production and cannot be denied. It remains to be studied whether there is a danger of extinction of fish species. The question of banning trap-netting, because it affects the lives of fishermen in Zhejiang Province, still needs to be considered. This is a pending case. To solve it, we must still explore the root of the problem in the fishing method to avoid hindering the main issue under the principle of reproduction.
