Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Factory: Promoters' Meeting 138

Share payments limited to the end of May; Inaugural meeting scheduled for June 8th

The Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Factory, since last year, had 200,000 yuan allocated by the Jiangxi Provincial Government as initial capital. The remaining 800,000 yuan was to be raised by Mr. Du Chongyuan. Since the fundraising and preparation began, progress has been reported in this newspaper. Regarding the Shanghai share payments, due to tight financial conditions among Shanghai merchants, although 400,000 yuan in commercial shares had been raised, they could not be fully paid up immediately. When Mr. Du Chongyuan returned to Jiangxi at the beginning of last month, Minister Kong, Li Shizeng, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Gongquan, and leaders from Shanghai's financial and industrial circles jointly sent a letter to Jiangxi Chairman Xiong Tianyi, reporting on the Shanghai share fundraising situation, with Kong, Li, Du, and Zhang undertaking to collect the 400,000 yuan in share payments and remit them within a short period. After Mr. Du Chongyuan returned to Jiangxi, he surveyed factory sites, supervised factory construction, and trained workers, preparing to commence operations. Recently, with factory affairs arranged, he returned to Shanghai to discuss the collection of share payments with the promoters. Yesterday, at 1 PM, Minister Kong, Song Ziwen, Mayor Wu, Li Shizeng, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Zhou Zuomin, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Gongquan, Xu Jiying, Wu Yunzhai, and Du Chongyuan, among others, hosted a banquet at the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road for the shareholders, with over twenty guests in attendance. It was resolved that all share payments must be made in full by the end of this month, and the inaugural meeting would be held on June 8th. Details are as follows:

Minister Kong's Speech: Westerners call porcelain "China." If we cherish porcelain, it is equivalent to loving our country. Jiangxi's porcelain industry was once world-renowned, but due to a lack of innovation, it gradually fell behind, allowing foreign porcelain to increasingly penetrate the market. The extent of the outflow of wealth is alarming. However, due to a lack of specialized talent, improvement was impossible. The year before last, Mr. Du Chongyuan came to Shanghai, proposing a plan to establish a large-scale porcelain factory in China. Mr. Du originally ran a porcelain factory in the Northeast with excellent results. Within a few years, he managed to suppress foreign porcelain to the point where it could not be sold. I believe everyone is familiar with Mr. Du's experience in establishing a porcelain factory in the Northeast, so I won't reintroduce it. Fortunately, the Jiangxi Provincial Government, because the Red bandits within the province were suppressed last year, strived for construction and very much wanted to improve the Jiangxi porcelain industry. I then introduced Mr. Du to Jiangxi to discuss the matter. The Jiangxi Provincial Government, despite financial difficulties, was able to allocate 200,000 yuan from the provincial treasury to start the porcelain factory, which is truly commendable. Since everyone in Shanghai was previously supportive, I hope everyone will continue to encourage each other and pay up their shares as soon as possible, so that the fundraising can be completed and the company can open early. This is not a solicitation for donations. When the porcelain factory is established in the future, everyone will benefit. For example, the porcelain used in the International Hotel is entirely foreign-made. This is not only an economic outflow, but also a disgrace to our production sector. I hope that when the shareholders of our Guangda Porcelain Factory come to the International Hotel for meetings in the future, the porcelain used will be entirely from the Guangda Porcelain Factory. Now, I would like to invite Mr. Du Chongyuan to report.

Mr. Du's Report: Mr. Du Chongyuan rose and reported, stating, "Minister Kong has already spoken generally about the importance of the porcelain industry and the establishment of the porcelain factory. I also gave a more detailed report at the previous World Society meeting. What I want to report now is a brief review of the changes during the factory establishment period and the recent situation. I originally planned to establish a porcelain factory in Shanghai, initiated by Mr. Li Shizeng and Mr. Zhang Gongquan to raise shares. Later, because Minister Kong introduced me to Jiangxi, I canceled the original plan. During the negotiations with the Jiangxi Provincial Government, the Jiangxi Provincial Government initially advocated for government supervision and commercial operation, then government-commercial joint operation, and finally decided on complete commercial operation. As for the allocation of shares, the Jiangxi Provincial Government allocated 200,000 yuan as commercial shares, and I was responsible for raising the remaining 800,000 yuan. In the winter of last year, I raised 200,000 yuan in the Pingjin area and planned to raise 400,000 yuan in Shanghai, with the remaining 200,000 yuan to be raised in Hankou, Changsha, Shandong, and Shaanxi provinces. Now, the Jiangxi Provincial Government has allocated more than 200,000 yuan, and most of the share payments from various parties have been received. The 400,000 yuan in Shanghai shares have not been paid up because this year is a period of unusually tight financial conditions, unlike previous years. When I returned to Jiangxi last time, I discussed with the promoters and was instructed to return to Jiangxi first to prepare everything, and the share payments would be paid later. After I returned to Jiangxi, I began to reorganize Jiangxi porcelain through the Pottery Industry Administration and transferred important staff from the Northeast Porcelain Factory to plan and arrange everything. This time, my return to Shanghai is short, and I cannot negotiate everywhere, which I regret very much. As for how to raise the share payments, everyone present today is an important leader in the financial and industrial sectors, and I hope we can jointly agree on a solution, which I greatly appreciate."

Resolutions: After discussion among the promoters and shareholders, three resolutions were passed: (1) All share payments must be paid in full before the end of May. (2) The collection of share payments will be the responsibility of Zhang Gongquan, Qian Xinzhi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and Li Shizeng. (3) The inaugural meeting will be held at 2 PM on June 8th at the World Society at 393 Fookaisen Road. All of the above resolutions were passed and will be implemented separately. The meeting adjourned at 3 PM.

List of Share Subscriptions: The names of the subscribers in Shanghai and their subscription amounts for the Guangda Porcelain Factory are disclosed below: Kong Yongzhi: 40,000 yuan, Song Ziwen: 10,000 yuan, Wu Tiecheng: 10,000 yuan, Li Shizeng: 40,000 yuan, Zhang Gongquan: 40,000 yuan, Zhou Zuomin: 40,000 yuan, Hu Bijang: 20,000 yuan, Qian Xinzhi: 10,000 yuan, Du Yuesheng: 20,000 yuan, Zhang Xiaolin: 20,000 yuan, Xu Jiying: 10,000 yuan, Tang Shoumin: 10,000 yuan, Han Zhoubo: 20,000 yuan, Fang Yexian: 10,000 yuan, Xu Jingren & Wang Yiting: 1,000 yuan, Guo Shun: 2,000 yuan, Shi Yonggeng: 30,000 yuan, Mu Ouchu: 20,000 yuan, Cai Xiangquan: 5,000 yuan, Jin Tingsun: 5,000 yuan, Zhang Weiru: 10,000 yuan, Wu Yunchu: 2,000 yuan, Xu Taitang: 5,000 yuan, totaling 400,000 yuan.

The City Health Bureau recently received an order from the Municipal Government, which relayed a telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek: "It has been found that in various provinces and cities, Western doctors and dentists without licenses are practicing medicine, which is extremely harmful to the health of the people. Local public security bureau chiefs and health authorities should be responsible for personally inspecting them once a week to check whether all their equipment and instruments are clean and legal. American Protestant Episcopal Church to Build Large-Scale Hospital in Shanghai 142

Budget Set at US$500,000; St. Luke's and St. Elizabeth's Hospitals to Merge

The American Protestant Episcopal Church has two hospitals in Shanghai, St. Luke's and St. Elizabeth's. The church has raised US$500,000 to build another large-scale hospital in Shanghai, planning to merge St. Luke's and St. Elizabeth's. Details are as follows:

Budget of US$500,000: According to Bishop Guo of St. John's University of the Episcopal Church, the Council of the American Episcopal Church believes that hygiene facilities in China are still very rudimentary, and has decided to build a large-scale hospital in Shanghai, with a budget of US$500,000, which has been fully raised. It also plans to establish a nursing school within the hospital to cultivate nursing talent. After the American archbishop comes to Shanghai, bidding will be opened for construction.

New Hospital to Be Eight Stories: The hospital to be built by the Episcopal Church this time will be eight stories high. The site has been determined at the corner of Hardoon Road and Changping Road. The hospital will have 270 beds, and the eighth floor is reserved for an obstetrics hospital. In addition to the medical equipment provided by St. Luke's and St. Elizabeth's hospitals, new equipment will be purchased. St. Luke's Hospital has approximately one million yuan remaining from previous years, which can be used for equipment expenses. Therefore, after the hospital is established, it will be very large in scale.

St. Elizabeth's and St. Luke's to Merge: St. Elizabeth's and St. Luke's hospitals in Shanghai were established in 1880, and have a long history of 55 years. After the new hospital is completed, it is planned to merge the two hospitals into the new hospital. The original St. Luke's hospital will be used as an emergency room and ambulance station, and St. Elizabeth's Hospital on Avenue Road will be converted into an obstetrics hospital. Some medical equipment is prepared to be transferred to the new hospital for use. This plan has been confirmed by the American headquarters.

Cathay Theater to Show Film Celebrating the Accession of the British Monarch 143

A Page of 25 Years of British History

To commemorate the 25th anniversary of the accession of King George V of England, grand celebrations are being held everywhere. The Cathay Theater on the south bank of the Second Bridge will show "A 25-Year History of England" at 9:15 PM on the 8th to express its congratulations. This film is a joint production of all the British film companies, specially produced to commemorate the 25th anniversary of the British monarch's accession. All staff members were mobilized, with 200 main actors and 5 directors, setting an unprecedented record in British film history. The entire plot takes the British monarch as the warp and the events of the past 25 years in England as the weft, touching on local customs and the increasing changes, which is extremely interesting. By watching this film, the changes and evolution of England in the past 25 years are vividly displayed, making it a page of modern history, the value of which is extremely precious. All major events occurring from 1910 to 1935 are outlined in detail and vividly narrated. On the day the film was completed, the company immediately printed copies and shipped them to British locations around the world. For long distances, they were shipped by plane. The copies for Shanghai and Hong Kong were delivered by plane, first arriving in Singapore and then being transferred from Singapore to Shanghai. The shipping cost for this leg alone was 60 British pounds, showing the extent of their willingness to sacrifice. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion on the day the film is shown.

Inmates of the Special No. 2 Court Disobey Transfer and Commit Assault 147

Interrogated Separately Yesterday; Conflicting Testimonies from Inmates

Thirteen inmates of the detention center of the Special No. 2 Court, located in the east section of the Special Prison on Rue Massenet, including Wang Guinian, Qi Xingshun, Chen Xiaoyi, Liu Sheng, Zhang Jinding, Lu Sanxi, Yao Fushou, Xue Hongqing, Xu Debiao, and Li Zhendian, were ordered by the three directors of the detention center, Bai, Cai, and Wen, at 4 PM on the 9th of last month, to switch prison cells and return to the west section. Unexpectedly, the inmates refused to comply and resisted, using glass bottles to attack the guards. Director Sun Xiong rushed to stop them and was even attacked by Sun. When prison guard Zhang He stepped forward to protect Director Sun, he was wounded in the leg by the inmates, causing bleeding. The three ringleaders, Wang, Qi, and Chen, smashed their rice bowls, cut their own foreheads, and claimed that they were beaten by the guards with wooden sticks. Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan of the Special No. 2 Court was alerted and rushed to persuade them, but the inmates ignored the law. He summoned the guards and finally sent the inmates to the police station. The disturbance subsided. The next day, they were sent back and the inmates were shackled with heavy chains and transferred to the west section. The inmates then caused a commotion because their breakfast was [blank]. The inmates were transferred to the Procuratorate of the Special No. 2 Court. Chief Prosecutor Chen opened a court and ordered them to be detained for further investigation. Details have been reported in this newspaper. The case has been investigated by the Procuratorate, and a public prosecution has been filed on charges of obstructing official duties and causing injury. At 10:30 AM yesterday, Judge Li Changnian of the Special No. 2 Court opened the Third Criminal Court to interrogate the inmates. After the prosecutor Wang Ren stated the intention to prosecute, the judge ordered the inmates to be interrogated separately. The inmates all made excuses and denied disobeying orders and causing a commotion, claiming that they were beaten by the guards. After reviewing the testimonies, the court announced the conclusion and scheduled the trial for the 13th before [blank]. Afterwards, when the inmates were escorted back to the detention center, they requested to have their shackles removed before entering the prison. After the detention center staff tried their best to persuade them, the inmates finally entered [blank].

Huge Liner of Da Lai Company Crushes Five Dock Boats; Uncontrollable Due to Rapid Tide 148

Yesterday morning at 4 AM, a giant liner of the World Class of Da Lai Company arrived in Shanghai. When it approached the Longmao Dock on the Pudong Lujiazui waterfront, due to the rapid tide at that time and the large size of the ship, it was uncontrollable and went straight to the waterfront, causing all five empty dock boats berthed at the dock to be crushed. Boat No. 8204, owned by Chen Asheng, was damaged in the stern, with a loss of about 400 yuan. Boat No. 8807, owned by Xu Jinsheng, had the front of the oar and three beam feet damaged, with a loss of more than 100 yuan. Boat No. 9419, owned by Cao Guanquan, was damaged in the stern, with a loss of more than 100 yuan. Boat No. 7279, owned by Yang Linsheng, had the ship's stern canopy damaged, with a loss of more than 100 yuan. Boat No. 8461, owned by Zhang Fuhai, had the guardrail wood, the stern corner canopy, etc., damaged, with a loss of more than 100 yuan. Afterwards, the victims reported the incident to the Customs Water Police Station so that they could claim compensation from the shipping company for the losses.

Accused of Defrauding Money by Borrowing from Buddha; Cihang Pudu Ten Buddha Hall Swindles Wang Widow out of $1,000 152

Tang Fuhai, Tian Qiyu, and others from Jiangbei are devout believers in gods and Buddhas. In December of last year, they raised funds and built three bungalows in the North Tanjia Ferry area of West Shanghai, where they sculpted three golden statues of Guanyin Buddha and named the place Cihang Pudu Ten Buddha Hall. Tang and others burned incense and worshipped, chanting sutras day and night. In January of this year, Xue Hui and Wang Dexing falsely claimed to Tang and others that they were living Buddhas who had descended to earth, able to enlighten the masses and possessed various secret incantations to cure diseases with miraculous results. They said that if they could cooperate, they would surely become prosperous in the future. Tang and others believed them to be true and invited Xue and Wang to cooperate. Xue then went out to promote their cause. Before long, a general crowd of ignorant men and women arrived at the hall to burn incense and seek treatment for their illnesses. Whenever someone sought treatment and kowtowed, Xue would chant incantations silently and then give them ash water, claiming that it was immortal water and charging a few dollars. Unexpectedly, over time, more and more people sought help, and the place became very crowded. Xue and Wang, seeing that the villagers were gullible, boldly extorted money. A Yu woman, seeking treatment for her illness, was swindled out of $1,000 by Xue. Xue then took the money and claimed it for himself. Seeing that Tang and others were weak and easily bullied, he took over the place. Tang and others became extremely resentful and filed a complaint with the Caodu Public Security Sub-Bureau the other day. Yesterday, Director Wang sent police officer Liu Pei, accompanied by police chief Hu Fuzhong, to investigate the hall and found the claims to be true. They arrested Tang, Tian, Xue, and Wang for setting up a temple without authorization and defrauding people of money, and confiscated the Buddha statues and paper cylinders. After the bureau staff questioned them separately, they decided that the case was related to setting up a temple and defrauding people of money, and ordered them to be sent to the General Bureau for further investigation.

Jisheng Society Reports on Liyang Disaster, Requests Increased Relief Funds 156

The Chinese Jisheng Society, along with other charitable organizations such as the Sino-Foreign Relief Committee, jointly organized spring relief efforts in Liyang. Director Li Yunmen was publicly dispatched, accompanied by relief workers, to investigate and decided to take responsibility for the first, second, third, and sixth districts of the county, conducting investigations separately. According to the director's report, Liyang has suffered from years of famine, war disasters, banditry, and financial losses. Last year, it suffered another severe drought. Over one million mu of paddy fields throughout the county suffered complete crop failure. The county is divided into six districts. Except for the fourth and fifth districts, which are being handled by the Wuxi Red Swastika Society, the first, second, third, and sixth districts have been inspected by the Sino-Foreign Relief Committee and the Jisheng Society. The sixth district is the most severely affected, being high in altitude and mountainous. The first, second, and third districts are slightly less severe. The suffering people are on the verge of death. They have pawned or sold everything. They are temporarily sustaining their lives on "Guanyin flour," bran, tree bark, and grass roots. It is said that "Guanyin flour" is actually fossilized stone, which causes severe intestinal pain after consumption, leading to countless deaths. Furthermore, those who fled to other places last winter to seek food are now returning due to the relief efforts, bringing their elderly and children, one after another. Dogs are nowhere to be seen in the villages they pass through, no chickens are heard, and no smoke rises from the chimneys. The situation is extremely dire. A sudden frost and snow fell last month, severely damaging the mulberry gardens and wheat crops. Natural disasters and human calamities are difficult to reverse. The society is responsible for the first, second, third, and sixth districts, which have more than 70,000 affected households, with a population of over 200,000 people, crying out for food and unable to survive without relief. It is estimated that there are over 50,000 households. According to the original relief funds, the resources are too meager to effectively distribute among so many people. Each incense officer constantly sends letters requesting an increase in relief tickets, which requires an increase in relief funds. Even after reducing the amount for the less severely affected, adhering to the principle of saving lives rather than alleviating poverty, many are disappointed. The overall plea is for increased funds to save these surviving people. The director witnessed the suffering firsthand and requested that the Sino-Foreign Relief Committee and other charitable organizations be implored to generously provide compassion during this most difficult time between harvests, jointly increase their efforts, and add even one more yuan, as it could save a life and create immeasurable blessings. In the past, the disasters in Shaanxi and Henan were the most severe. Now, the natural disasters have shifted to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang regions. Saving lives is an urgent matter, and those who want to live cannot. It is hoped that all the great philanthropists at home and abroad will be inspired to save lives at this critical juncture, and the merit will be ten times greater than usual.

Red Swastika Society Organizes Spring Relief Efforts in Jiangsu and Jiangxi Provinces, Raising Over 100,000 Yuan in Relief Funds 157

The Red Swastika Society achieved considerable success in organizing relief efforts in Jiangsu and Jiangxi provinces last year. It is reported that the society is now raising over 100,000 yuan in relief funds to continue spring relief efforts. A summary of the society's relief efforts in various regions is detailed below.

Relief Efforts in Jiangsu Province: The disaster area in Jiangsu Province that is the most affected is Liyang. The Red Swastika Society is responsible for the fourth and fifth districts, allocating 40,000 yuan. Tang Huiqing and others from the Wuxi Red Swastika Society purchased 140,000 pieces of bean cakes, each weighing nine catties and four ounces, for distribution. They also allocated 4,000 yuan. Hua Jingxiu from the Wuxi Red Swastika Society personally went to the county to discuss purchasing two types of seeds, sheep willow and broadleaf, to be distributed by the Drought Relief Association. The disaster situation in Wuxi is also severe. Chairman Cai Quchen of the Wuxi branch is working with local authorities to raise 10,000 shi of foreign rice. The Ministry of Finance has approved and issued a duty-free passport for this purpose. Additionally, 1,000 yuan each was provided to Yizheng and Liuhe counties for spring relief.

Relief Efforts in Jiangxi Province: Zhao Yulin, the captain of the Second Relief Team of the Red Swastika Society, reported that 400 shi of rice has been allocated to the disaster area of Nanfeng, and distribution in the seventh district has been completed. The fifth and sixth districts are currently under investigation. The disaster situation in Nancheng is relatively mild, and distribution in the second and sixth districts has been scheduled. The disaster situation in Lichuan is extremely severe, with starving people everywhere. The county has six districts. According to the "strict and lenient distribution" method, 800 shi of relief rice was allocated, which should be enough to provide universal relief. The districts are currently being investigated. In areas with rugged roads and inconvenient transportation, rice has been purchased nearby for distribution. In addition, Poyang suffered from hail damage, destroying the wheat crops. The disaster victims are in dire need of relief. The Red Swastika Society has allocated 300 shi of emergency relief rice. Another 300 shi of emergency relief rice has been allocated to Donggu Town in Ji'an. As for the relief efforts in Gao'an, they have already begun, with the two team leaders, Hong Chenglin and Hu Zhongcheng, working with local communities to manage the process.

Selling Dried Tobacco: Zhang Jiangshan Drowns in the River 158

Zhang Jiangshan from Zhenjiang, age thirty-six, recently opened a Dadesheng dried tobacco shop at number 266 Linping Road, Xiangyan Bridge, Hongkou, specializing in wholesale business. The day before yesterday in the early morning, Zhang Jiangshan and the shop clerk Yan Guozhen, each carrying two shoulder poles, transported 2,200 packages of dried tobacco by ferry from Dongjiadu to Tangqiao Town in Pudong. They sold dried tobacco to various grocery stores, sometimes dozens of packages, sometimes one or two hundred packages. They gradually moved to Yangjiadu Town, having sold a total of 750 packages. At about 11:30 AM, Zhang Jiangshan, with the remaining goods, intended to sell them in the Nanshi area. Thus, he and the shop clerk Yan Guozhen boarded the Yangjiadu ferry (which uses a small boat for towing). Because it was noon, there were fewer passengers, so there were five empty ferries docked at the pier. Passengers had to cross over these empty boats to board. The empty boat on the outside would then take passengers in turn. Zhang Jiangshan was the first to step onto Gu Hongsheng's ferry. Subsequently, Yan Guozhen, carrying the tobacco basket on his shoulder, followed him onto the boat. He lost his footing and fell into the river. Zhang Jiangshan, in an attempt to help Yan Guozhen, also fell into the water. Gu Hongsheng, the owner of the ferry, saw the accident and quickly called his companions to rescue them. They managed to rescue Yan Guozhen, saving him from drowning. However, Zhang Jiangshan did not resurface after falling into the river and apparently drowned. The body's whereabouts are unknown and efforts to locate it have been unsuccessful. The shoulder pole and over a thousand packages of dried tobacco had already scattered and drifted away. Afterwards, Gu Hongsheng, the owner of the ferry, and Yan Guozhen went to the water patrol station to report the incident and request the recovery of the body. According to Yan Guozhen, "When I stepped onto the ferry, I fell into the river. The shop owner Zhang Jiangshan helped me, causing him to fall into the river and drown." Yesterday afternoon, the detective summoned Zhang Jiangshan's wife, Zhang Jiangshi, and briefly questioned Yan Guozhen and Zhang Jiangshi, before handing them over to the local court for interrogation. Meanwhile, patrol boats were ordered to search for the body at the scene of the incident. The deceased was wearing a blue lined spring robe, a black lined spring jacket, black cloth shoes, and black lined trousers. As of yesterday evening, the body had not been recovered.

Woman Commits Suicide by Taking Three Bottles of Miltown 159

Huang Canhui, age twenty-eight, from Guangdong, is the owner of the Meihua Art Advertising Agency at number 47 Wufu Lane, Nanjing Road. His wife, Ms. Lu, also age twenty-eight and also from Guangdong, named Yuqing, had been married for a long time but had not yet given birth. Recently, Huang's advertising agency failed, resulting in losses. According to Ms. Lu's intentions, Huang's depression led to a rash decision. On the afternoon of the 4th at 11 PM, she went alone to the Dafang Hotel on Zhengjia Muqiao Street in the French Concession and registered under her own name, Lu Yuqing, for room 107 on the second floor. After booking the room, she went to the bathroom to take a bath. After finishing, she returned to the room, put on makeup, powdered her face, put fresh flowers in her hair, dressed neatly, and swallowed three bottles of Miltown sleeping pills, committing suicide. After taking the pills, she closed the door, lay down on the bed, and waited for death. At approximately 6 AM the next morning, the poisoning caused her to moan, which was discovered by the tea attendant Shi Rumei (age forty, from Shaoxing). He entered the room and reported it to the French police, who immediately summoned an ambulance to take her to Renji Hospital. Due to severe poisoning, treatment was ineffective, and she died at 1:41 PM. The hospital notified the French police, who sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Zhuan Yuan Branch Hall for examination. Yesterday morning, the deceased's husband, Huang Canhui, learned of the news, rushed to the mortuary to identify the body, and wept bitterly over the corpse. Subsequently, the police reported to the Second Special District Court Procuratorate, which dispatched Inspector Wang Ren and forensic doctor Jiang Zhao, and other officials to the mortuary at noon to confirm that the deceased had indeed died from poisoning before death. The officials questioned the tea attendant Shi Rumei and the deceased's husband, before ruling that the body could be claimed by the husband upon signing a guarantee for burial.

How should this be handled? The resolution was passed, complying with the previous resolution: "Anyone who has not paid membership fees or completed the membership formalities will be deemed to have forfeited their membership." Those who report after the deadline will be considered members after the founding meeting and will have no voting rights. The meeting adjourned.

Fake "Three Wheels" Brand Products of Lianhua Factory Found, Factory Will Strictly Investigate 162

The Lianhua Woolen Mill, located in Hele Lane, North Henan Road, has been in operation for over ten years. Its products, mainly "Three Wheels" brand high-quality silk men's socks and wool swimsuits, are popular among major companies and department stores nationwide. Because they are durable and retain their appearance, they are very different from ordinary products on the market. Therefore, sales are very prosperous. However, recently, unscrupulous people have coveted the factory's business, using the word "zhuan" to create a "Three Wheels" brand form in an attempt to imitate and deceive consumers. It is reported that the factory owner, in order to maintain the reputation of the "Three Wheels" brand, will find ways to conduct a thorough investigation.

He has now opened Gongjian Hospital at number 208 Baike Road. The equipment is complete, and the technology is excellent. Recently, due to strict anti-smoking measures, he has established a special anti-smoking department to serve the community, adopting scientific methods for fundamental treatment and not prioritizing profit. Therefore, the prices are extremely low, which is greatly praised by patients.

Meeting Record of Yimiao Yu Garden National Products Association 165

The Yimiao Yu Garden Merchants' Association for the Promotion of National Products held its sixth executive committee standing committee meeting the night before last. Yang Zhitian was publicly elected as chairman, and the meeting proceeded according to protocol. Matters for discussion included: (1) Chairman's report; (2) Yu Garden stallholders came to the meeting in succession to express their views. The area is thriving, and the stalls are densely packed. Although business is slow due to the current situation, they are determined to maintain it and hope to revive it. They reported that opening the garden and cracking down on stalls would cut off the livelihood of the masses. They urgently requested relief. Resolved: Submit a petition to the Municipal Party Department, requesting it to forward the matter to the competent authorities, considering the livelihood of the people and exempting them from the crackdown; (3) Shop members believe that if the crackdown on vendors is unfortunately implemented, the market will inevitably become even more depressed, and business will definitely suffer a major blow. Upon hearing this bad news, everyone panicked and came to the association to request remedial measures. Please make a public decision. Resolved: To be handled together with the previous case; (4) Omitted; (5) Secret. The meeting adjourned after discussions.

City Sounds 168

Hongzhang Silk Fabric Store to Auction Off Inventory: Hongzhang Silk Fabric Store on Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen, has been closed for many months due to the impact of the market. It is reported that in order to quickly close down, the store has decided to hold a clearance auction of more than 100,000 items of inventory, regardless of cost, starting on the 10th of this month.

Zhao, a Prisoner, is Sentenced; Chen Jinlan is Sentenced to Four Years of Imprisonment; Wang Afu is Sentenced for Lending Money 169

Chen Jinlan from Ningbo, a prisoner detained in the Second Special District Local Court Detention Center for murder, was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment after being upheld by the Supreme Court in the third trial. When the Third Branch Court received the verdict and was about to send her to prison, she escaped from prison on the morning of December 27th of the previous year at approximately 1 AM, taking advantage of the guards' negligence and using a wire to open the inner and outer prison doors. The Procuratorate of the High Third Branch Court issued an arrest warrant. On the afternoon of the 15th of last month at 4 PM, Bao Dongliang and Yang Zhongfang, detectives from the French Police Department, learned that after Chen escaped, she fled to Hankou. Unable to make a living, she returned to Shanghai and hid in the home of Bian Wuchang, a fellow villager on the front floor of a carpentry shop at number 32 Lao Yong'an Street. They immediately went to the address, arrested Chen, and arrested Wang Afu from Suzhou, who had lent money to Chen to help her hide. They were escorted to the Second Special District Court, where the prosecutor and the police department separately filed public prosecutions for the crimes of escape and harboring a criminal. The circumstances of the trial have been reported in this newspaper. After a final trial by Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special District Court, Judge Zhang went to the First Criminal Court yesterday morning at 10 AM and ordered Chen and Wang to be brought to the court. Chen Jinlan was sentenced to four years of imprisonment for damaging the implements of the detention facility and escaping, and Wang Afu was sentenced to two years of imprisonment for enabling an escapee to hide. The number of days of detention before sentencing will be offset by two days for each day of imprisonment. After the sentencing, Chen requested the court to return the five yuan in banknotes that were confiscated from her when she was arrested. The court stated that the money was lent to Chen by an informant who was paid by the detectives handling the case and denied her request. Chen cursed the court and was taken back to the detention center by the bailiff to await further action.

The China Anti-Smoking Association Offers Free Smoking Cessation: Smoking not only harms the body and wastes money but also harms society to no small extent. In this time of economic downturn, there are many who want to quit but struggle financially. In light of this, the China Anti-Smoking Association, founded by prominent figures such as Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Fudeng, Hu Yongqi, Hong Yanbin, Shi Zhikun, Hu Juewen, and Chen Xiaowei, is conducting free smoking cessation to benefit the poor and sick. Detailed regulations are available. Send a letter with four cents postage, and it will be mailed to you. The address is 466 Dongsi Road, Shilu Road.

Publishing Industry 171

National Defense Forum Bi-Monthly Air Defense Special Issue: Since its reform, the National Defense Forum bi-monthly has greatly improved its content and frequently publishes special issues to discuss various important issues related to national defense. It is truly the best publication in the country for studying national defense. The previously published issue on the Sino-Japanese problem and the petroleum special issue received favorable reviews from the general public. The colleagues of the society are continuing to work hard and dare not slack off. The recently published air defense special issue is even more exciting. In the future, they will continue to publish special issues on border areas, highways, etc. Anyone who wants to read this type of publication quickly can subscribe directly to the National Defense Forum Society at number 24, Garden Villa, Huanlong Road, Shanghai. Attach seven cents postage. You can also read a trial copy.

Blood Flower Collection: The recent collection of poems "Blood Flower" by young writer Ge Chongfei was published yesterday. The words are beneficial to the public, and the illustrations are profound and interesting. All major bookstores sell it. If you enclose a four-cent postage stamp and send it to the Literature and Art Society, number 63 Pushi Road, this city, you will receive a copy of this book signed by the author himself.

Free "Meiyingxuan Manuscripts": Pan Junchuan, a poet from Yuezhong, was knowledgeable at a young age and devoted himself to poetry. Unfortunately, heaven did not grant him many years, and he suddenly passed away. His book "Meiyingxuan Manuscripts" was revised and published by his friend Gao Tianqi. It consists of four volumes, with a total of one hundred and twenty-seven items. It is exquisitely printed on traditional Chinese Lian Shi paper in antique style and is offered free of charge to those who share the same interest. The first and second editions have already been given away, and requests from various places continue to pour in. The third edition has now been published. If you wish to obtain the collection, please enclose an eight-cent postage stamp and send it to Gao Tianqi, Tianyi Film Company, number 232 Ganshidong Road, French Concession, Shanghai, and a copy will be sent to you.

Nüsheng Society Has Moved to the Cultural Street: The Nüsheng Society has been around for over three years since its formation. Since leaving the Christian Women's Temperance Union in June of last year, the society has been led by the first-rate and most progressive female writers in the country. The Nüsheng bi-monthly, which it publishes, has also become increasingly popular among readers due to its independent, pure stance and rich and substantial content. The business has expanded rapidly. Recently, in order to adapt to the operation, facilitate distribution, and maintain close relationships with the majority of readers, the society's general distribution office and editorial department have all been moved to number 286, next to the Modern Bookstore, Zhongsi Road, yesterday morning.

Weather Report 173

According to the meteorological forecast issued by the Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday, the area around Shandong is cloudy and clear, with rather strong and sharp winds from no fixed direction, due to a low-pressure system passing through Mongolia and moving eastward. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy with fog, with winds from the northeast to northwest. The East China Sea has gentle winds and possibly rain or fog, due to a small low-pressure system passing through and moving northeast-east. Furthermore, the highest temperature in this city within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 69.3 degrees, and the lowest was 58.5 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 79.5 degrees, and the lowest was 57.9 degrees.

Special Notice

Report on the Business of the Bank of Communications (9) 175

(3) Business in the Jiangbei Area: The Jiangbei area south of the river is a production area for cotton, grains, and miscellaneous crops, and commerce is traditionally prosperous. In order to promote business, the bank has successively established branches in Dongtai, Lincheng, Rufou, Huai'an, Gaoyou, Jiangyan, Shentong, Shiying, Taixing, Huangqiao, and other places to actively conduct business, which has been quite fruitful.

(4) Adding Warehouses: In order to provide credit based on goods, it is necessary to establish warehouses. The bank already has warehouses in places such as Shanghai, Nanjing, Qingdao, Xuzhou, Bengbu, Changshu, Ningbo, and other places, which are already of considerable scale. However, those already established still need to be expanded, and those not yet established urgently need to be added. In this fiscal year, efforts have been made in this regard, and preparations have been made in various commodity distribution centers, either by purchasing land for self-construction, renting houses for trial operation, cooperating with other banks, or operating independently by the bank, all depending on the local situation, with a degree of flexibility. It is estimated that within one year, the number of newly added and expanded warehouses has reached seventy-seven, including eighteen warehouses, thirty-eight sub-warehouses, and twenty-one specially contracted warehouses. The main items stored are cotton yarn, rice, wheat, silk, ramie, peanuts, miscellaneous grains, flour, hides, and furs. The distribution locations of each warehouse are listed as follows:

List of Schools Participating in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Private Middle School Sports Meet, Track and Field and Volleyball Events to Be Held in Suzhou Starting on the 10th 176

Suzhou Express News: The annual Jiangsu-Zhejiang Private Middle School Sports Meet (8th session) is being hosted by Suzhou Yancheng Middle School. Preparations have been completed, and it is scheduled to be held for three days from the 10th to the 13th of this month. The venues are Tianci Village, Soochow University, for track and field events, and Yancheng for volleyball and tennis. The opening ceremony will be held at 9:00 AM on the 10th, followed by track and field competitions starting at 1:00 PM in the afternoon, with volleyball and tennis held at the same time. The chairman of the organizing committee is Feng Jiaozhun, director of physical education at Yancheng, and Zhang Hanwei, county magistrate of Wu County, Yang Yongqi, president of Soochow University, Chen Zichu, principal of Yancheng, and Dr. Mai Jiaqi, founder of the school, have been invited to serve as honorary vice-chairmen. The chief referee is Jiang Xiangqing, the head referee for field events is Zhang Nianzu, the head referee for track events is Ma Zhikui, the head referee for volleyball is Feng Bingxin, and the head referee for tennis is Huang Bobin. In order to maintain order at the venues, the organizing committee requires all attendees to enter with tickets, which cost two dimes apiece. This year, with the exception of Hangzhou Zhijiang, Zhejiang Lan, and Suzhou Cuiying, which are unable to participate and have withdrawn, the remaining eight schools, including Nanjing Jinling, Shanghai Hujiang, John, Mingqiang, Yinghua, Suzhou Soochow, and Taowu, have submitted their rosters, which were compiled and arranged by the organizing committee yesterday (6th). Jiangda Volleyball Finals: Fudan Retains Championship, Score 3-0, Jinan Loses Again 177

This year's Jiangda Volleyball Tournament, which began on April 30th, included Jinling and Central from Nanjing, and Guanghua, Chizhi, Fudan, and Jinan from Shanghai, a total of six schools. However, Jinling and Central both withdrew voluntarily due to unforeseen circumstances, so only the four Shanghai schools competed. After several days of competition, Fudan and Jinan won the right to compete in the finals. The two teams played the finals yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at the Chizhi Stadium. It is understood that Fudan is the volleyball champion of Jiangda, and its strength is very strong. Jinan also made every effort to attack, and although Xu Heng rushed back from Hangzhou to join the team, the whole team lacked coordination, and he had little support. As a result, Fudan relied on the spiking of Qiu, Chen, Zhou, and others to defeat Jinan 3-0 and retain the championship.

First Set

At the start of the match, Jinan's momentum was very strong. Xu Heng's blocking and spiking won three points in a row. Fudan's Qiu Guangxie, Zhou Dayun, and Chen Zongqi coordinated their attacks, spiking left and right, and in an instant, they won the switch with a score of 11-5. After switching sides, Fudan continued to improve and scored six points in one go. Jinan only scored one point, making the score 17-6. Jinan calmly responded and once revived its momentum, chasing the score to 17-10. However, Fudan's momentum did not wane, and Qiu and Chen made contributions with every move. Fudan then won the first set 21-10.

Second Set

Fudan became even more fierce, and Jinan was unwilling to give in. Fudan consistently led by two points. From then on, Fudan's momentum was overwhelming, and everything they sought was achieved easily. After 15-6, Jinan's Xu Heng, with the assistance of Wang Nanzhen, made the score 15-8. After that, Jinan made few gains, and Fudan's Qiu Guangxie's spiking was like the collapse of heaven and earth, which Jinan could not resist. They eventually lost again with a score of 11-21.

Third Set

After losing two sets in a row, Jinan's main player Xu Heng gathered the players and secretly gave instructions under the net. Sure enough, the team's morale was greatly boosted, and Xu Heng's setting and spiking gave them a three-point lead. Fudan's Qiu, Zhou, and Chen then showed their best skills, with arm spikes and blocks, achieving success naturally. After switching sides at 11-9, Jinan still thought of winning with surprise moves, and Xu Heng relied on his courage to pull back three points, but it was a drop in the bucket and ultimately failed to save the situation. They eventually lost 19-21.

Fudan

Zhou Jieming, Chen Zongqi, Chen Bocai

Zhou Dayun, Li Huihua, Zeng Qixiang

Situ Ting, Qiu Guangxie, Guan Yuan'an

Jinan

Wang Nanzhen, Guan Ruirui, Wu Zhifeng

Xu Heng, Li Qiyao, Zhang Zhimin

Kuang Yaozu, Li Jianxin, Ma Shaobang

Opening of the Junior Baseball League: John's Overwhelming Victory Over American School, 12-3, Today Hujiang vs. Jiaotong 178

The Shanghai Junior Baseball League, initiated by the Huadong Company, with the participation of John's, American School, Hujiang, and Jiaotong Universities, began yesterday afternoon. John's played against American School at the American School field on Beidang Road. As a result, John's won overwhelmingly by 12-3. Hujiang vs. Jiaotong will be held today at 4:00 PM at Jiaotong University in Xujiahui.

The situation was completely one-sided. John's was superior to American School in all aspects. John's pitcher, Gan Zhen, had decent technique, and although there were often four balls, American School players were often struck out and had to leave the field. The American School's pitcher was weak and unable to do much, reportedly due to a hand injury. John's had as many as four home runs. John's batted first and scored one point each in the second and third innings. In the fourth inning, a long ball flew into the flowers and trees, and three people ran in a row. This inning totaled as many as five points. After John's scored eight points, American School also got a home run in the sixth inning, only to add two more points. The Chinese Middle School Sports Federation: Track and Field Regularly Held: Date...This Month 24th and 25th; Location...Guanghua University on Great West Road 181

The Shanghai Middle School Sports Federation Track and Field Committee, with Jiang Jingnan (Chairman), Yu Jie, Wu Lisheng, and Lu Xiang (Qian Dai), held a meeting the day before yesterday at the Shenyuan Sports Association to prepare for the Sixth Middle School Track and Field Meet. The resolutions are recorded below:

(1) Date: In accordance with the decision of the general meeting, the date is set for May 24th and 25th (Friday and Saturday).

(2) Location: Guanghua University on Great West Road.

(3) Registration: Registration begins immediately and closes at 6:00 PM on the 15th of this month. Registration forms will be sent to each school separately. Please fill them out according to the format and send them to Jiang Nan, Chairman of the Track and Field Committee, Guanghua High School Affiliated to Guanghua University, Great West Road. Registration must be done by registered mail. Late registrations will not be accepted under any circumstances.

(4) Championship: Men's will have championships for both field events and track events. Women's will have a single track and field championship.

(5) Events: (A) Men's Field Events: Discus, 11-pound shot put, javelin, high jump, long jump, triple jump, pole vault; (B) Track Events: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1500 meters, 5000 meters, 200-meter intermediate hurdles (same distance and height as low hurdles), 400-meter relay, 1600-meter relay (relay not counted for points but prizes will be prepared separately); (C) Women's Track and Field: 90 meters, 100 meters, 200-meter relay, high jump, long jump, 8-pound shot put, softball throw, javelin (new event).

(6) Limits: Each school is limited to a maximum of four entries in each event. Each athlete, male or female, may participate in a maximum of four events and may not participate exclusively in field events or track events. Women may participate in a maximum of three events. Once events are confirmed, no changes or additions may be requested under any circumstances.

(7) Duties: Guanghua High School Affiliated to Guanghua University is entrusted with the preparation and planning of the venue. Jiang Jingnan will be responsible for competition arrangements, Wu Lisheng will be responsible for administration, and Yu Jie will be responsible for records. Referees will be jointly discussed and appointed by the committee members.

(8) Prizes: The association will purchase men's and women's championships and individual medals. At the same time, a general letter will be sent to various schools and organizations to solicit prizes. The award ceremony for all sports competitions championships held by the association throughout the year will be held during the track and field meet to show solemnity.

(9) Eligibility: 1. All participants must be amateur athletes. 2. Athletes must meet the following academic standards: (1) Athletes must be officially registered students of their respective schools and must be enrolled in at least twenty hours of classes per week at the school they represent. (Students enrolled in less than twenty hours of classes per week who wish to participate in competitions should first submit their cases to the representative meeting for a decision). (2) Students who fail more than one-third of their courses in a semester may not represent their school in any competitions organized by the association. Courses for which a passing grade has not yet been determined will also be considered failing. Students whose failing grades are due to illness or other legitimate reasons and who wish to participate in competitions must first submit their cases to the committee for review and a decision on their eligibility. (3) Students who represent one of the association's schools in a competition and then transfer to another school are not eligible to represent their school in competition for one semester after the transfer. However, students who transfer back to their original school after transferring are still eligible to continue participating in competitions. (4) Graduates who remain at school for remedial classes or research are not eligible to represent the school in competition. (5) Students may participate in competitions organized by the association for a maximum of six years. Using high school as a standard, the three years of high school are the final period during which an athlete may participate in competitions organized by the association. Thereafter, under no circumstances may they be reinstated as an athlete in the association. (6) Students may participate in a maximum of four sports per academic year.

Ministry Order: Xiamen University to Improve 185

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education instructed the private Xiamen University, stating in brief: According to the report from the Ministry's inspector, the teachers of the school are mostly full-time and dedicated to their work. Most of the students are able to be simple and studious, and abide by school rules. The reference books in each department and the scientific equipment of the College of Science are all of a considerable scale. The plant and animal specimens and research journals of the Department of Biology are quite rich. The department's emphasis on the study of local products is appropriate, and the discovery of *變形* [a technical term] is also of academic value. These achievements are commendable. However, the following points still need attention and improvement: 1. In recent years, the school's funding has been insufficient, and the allocation of expenditures, combined with the current state of school affairs, has failed to make sufficient progress. In the future, the board of directors should find ways to sort things out and raise a substantial fund to solidify the economic foundation. At the same time, the school should economize on administrative and miscellaneous expenses, and appropriately reduce the funding for the affiliated middle school, and increase the equipment expenses as much as possible to enrich the content and facilitate teaching. 2. The school's established curriculum is often changed during the course of studies, which has an impact. In the future, a detailed curriculum outline should be drawn up and implemented in earnest. 3. Attention should be paid to local teaching materials, such as the climate and customs of South China, the history, geography, dialects, business conditions, and international trade of Southeast Asia. 4. In the courses of the College of Liberal Arts and the College of Law and Commerce, which are biased towards lecturing, efforts should be made to guide students to conduct independent research. 5. Military training should be implemented in earnest. 6. The school's guidance facilities lack an active plan, the dormitory order is seldom clean and tidy, and there is no unified organization to handle student leave and absenteeism. It is necessary to establish responsible personnel to actively supervise and train them. 7. The staffing of the people in charge of the Finance Department and the Affairs Department is redundant and should be reduced. The Director of Group Education and the Group Education Staff should be changed to the Director of Student Affairs and the Student Affairs Staff respectively, in order to comply with the law. 8. The library has a small capacity and the layout is not entirely appropriate, and each department cannot make full use of it. Attention should be paid to improvement and promotion of practical efficiency. The school is hereby ordered to comply and report back.

Ministry of Education Explains: Physical Education School Exam Subjects and Class Types 186

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education ordered the departments and bureaus to handle six cases. According to the report from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, the private Shanghai Physical Education Normal School requested an explanation of the exam subjects, class types, and gymnastic movements for the entrance examination. The Ministry instructed: "The matter has been reported. The various movements of the political class in the examination subjects can be understood by referring to the detailed syllabus of physical education professors compiled by the Ministry. The term *變目動作、（經中側掛腿雖楦撐）* [ gymnastic movement, (although leg supports through the middle side of the last)] under the equipment section is relatively obscure. It is now changed to *腿離楦經中側撐、並附該節全部動作腿式圖三幅* [Legs leave the last, passing through the middle and supporting from the side, and three pictures of all the movements of that section are attached]. Please inform them to take note of this and so on." It is appropriate to record this case immediately and inform them and transfer it to the affiliated physical education normal schools or physical education normal departments.

After dinner at 8:00 PM, he watched a movie with the students. At 2:00 PM, he left Suqian and returned to Yunhe Station, and then went to Donghai.

Jiangsu Province Revises: Regulations on the Payment of Provincial Education Special Funds: Approved by the Provincial Government and Ordered to Be Followed by the Counties 189

The regulations for the payment of special education funds in Jiangsu Province have been in effect for a long time, but the collection procedures are still close to the border, and the audit is even more difficult. Now, the Provincial Education Funds Management Office and the Finance Department have revised the payment method, expanded the scope of the entire treasury, and formulated a full treasury report form to be filled out by the entire treasury on a daily basis for more accurate auditing. The various procedures are in line with the current full treasury system in Jiangsu Province. The regulations have now been approved by the provincial government and ordered to be followed by the counties with immediate effect. The regulations are listed below:

Article 1: The payment procedures for special provincial education funds shall be handled in accordance with these regulations. Article 2: After the counties collect the land tax portion of the special provincial education funds, they shall clearly divide it the next morning and handle the payment procedures. In special circumstances, or if the division is not possible, the provincial and county tax funds collected shall be deposited in the treasury bank for a maximum of ten days at a time, and shall be paid in full on a ten-day basis. Article 3: When counties pay the special education funds, the county magistrate shall fill out a payment form and submit it directly to the Education Funds Management Office for collection. Article 4: After the tooth tax and slaughter tax portions of the special provincial education funds are collected, they shall be clearly divided the next morning, and the special funds shall be deposited. A payment form shall be filled out on a monthly basis and submitted directly to the Education Funds Management Office for collection. Article 5: The provincial treasury shall also handle the payment of provincial education special funds by the bank acting as the provincial treasury on a daily basis. Article 6: The provincial treasury shall also fill out two copies of the report form for the receipt and payment of provincial education special funds on a daily basis, one copy to the Education Funds Management Office and one copy to the Finance Department for verification. Article 7: The Education Funds Management Office shall appoint commissioners to take turns going to the counties to supervise the county governments and various collection agencies to fulfill their responsibility of payment, without handling payment matters directly. Article 8: From the date of implementation of these regulations, all existing provincial education special funds payment procedures that conflict with these regulations shall be abolished. Article 9: These regulations shall be formulated jointly by the Finance Department and the Education Funds Management Office, and shall be implemented after being submitted to the provincial government for the record.

The Examination Group of the Secondary Normal Education Research Association Discusses the Issue of Abolishing the Examination: Presents Three Suggestions for Discussion by the General Assembly: The Research Results of Each Group Will Be Compiled into a Special Volume by the Bureau 191

The graduation examination group of the Shanghai Municipal Secondary Normal Education Research Association held its third research meeting yesterday afternoon at the Lake Society. Chen Ji-cheng, Tao Guang-chuan, Yang Dao-hong, Yu Xi-rong, Lu Zhong-da, Tang Nai-kang, Jin Yue-zhang, and Shen Ti-lan attended, as well as representatives Zhou Shang and Qian Fu-gong of the Bureau of Education. Chen Ji-cheng was the chairman and Tao Guang-chuan was the recorder. The results of the research problems were: (1) It was decided to add the first item of school performance standards to ensure more student graduation and to make school performance more accurate. (2) It was requested that the Ministry of Education issue a general order to all public and private universities in the country that all entrance examination questions for each subject should be in Chinese and should be based on the provisions of the syllabus standard promulgated by the Ministry to facilitate student advancement. (3) The issue of the abolition of the graduation examination. The previous meeting had put forward three opinions: A. Abolish the examination system and replace it with a spot-check system. B. Abolish the examination system and replace it with a national examination system. C. Abolish the examination system and find other methods to remedy it. At yesterday's meeting, the members expressed many opinions on this issue, which lasted for a long time. Because this matter is of great importance, after careful research by the members, it was decided to submit it to the general meeting for discussion. The meeting adjourned after the discussion. The meetings of each group of the association have now all concluded. All discussions have been reported to the Education Bureau one after another, compiled and printed into a special volume, and submitted for discussion at the members' meeting on the 15th of this month.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 195

— (Yan Mao-de)

If a person can do things without missing a single minute or second, then he will definitely gain a great advantage in his career. Napoleon himself once said that the reason he was able to defeat the Austrian army was that the Austrian soldiers did not understand the value of "five minutes." Every minute they missed was giving "misfortune" one more opportunity to take advantage of.

Nelson had a saying that can also serve as a model for young people in doing things. "The success of my life's work is that I always start one quarter of an hour early in everything I do."

The size of success will never exceed the size of your self-confidence. Napoleon's army would never have climbed over the Alps if Napoleon himself had thought it was too difficult. Similarly, in your life, if you have great doubts and distrust about your own abilities, then you will never be able to accomplish great things.

Night Fourth-Class Special Feature 196

— Shazhou

In these times, money is too tight, and everything that costs money has to be carefully calculated. Take this trip home from Shanghai, for example. I knew that there were several trains leaving Shanghai for the north every day, but the express train was too expensive, and the slow train was not economical in terms of time. Although I didn't have any urgent business that required me to rush back overnight, once a traveler is on the way home, no one doesn't hope to get home a moment sooner. After a lot of calculation, I finally decided to take the night fourth-class train at 0:50 AM, because the night fourth-class train is not slower than the express train, but the price is much cheaper. When I decided to take the night fourth-class train, I thought I was a shrewd person, but who knew that when I entered the platform and walked to the door of each car, there were people stopping me from boarding, saying, "There's no room for even one more person. Please go to another car to see." When I heard this, I didn't quite believe it, and looked straight into the car. Only when I saw that the car was indeed crowded with people did I suddenly realize that there were many more than just me who were so-called shrewd people. But no matter how crowded it was, not getting on the train was not an option. After turning around twice, I had to say many good things to the temporary guards at the car door before they allowed me to get on. When I got on the train and looked around, oh my God, not only was the car full of people, but the inside and outside of the toilets and both sides of the aisles were also full of people. What should I do? Move forward? Retreat? There was nowhere to go.

"Traveling is never comfortable. Let's just stand for a few hours." That's what I thought in my heart. At the same time, I saw that the people on this train were all as disheveled as I was. It seemed that they were all forced out by the economic downturn. Well, let the economic downturn drive us back to the poor and helpless countryside. We are all in the same boat!

Ah Chang 197

— Wu Yafei

Ah Chang was a laborer hired to oversee work at our home in the past. He was from Jiangbei, brought back by my grandmother's maternal uncle, Fu Xiang, when he went to Changxing to clear land. Ah Chang didn't have a surname; his original name was "Da Changzi." We thought it sounded too unpleasant, so we changed his name.

He stayed with our family for a good five or six years, helping us with work in the fields and on the mountains. His wages were, of course, very meager—explicitly three dollars a month. This person wasn't really necessary for our family; we could use him, but we could also do without him. So, keeping him was really out of pity for his homelessness and vagrancy.

He was quite young and didn't look too repulsive, and he had a good physique, but he was somewhat lazy. He ate an alarming amount, always four large bowls each meal. Two *sheng* of white rice wasn't enough to fill him for a day; he could eat plain rice without any dishes.

My sister and I didn't like him because he spoke in a pure Jiangbei dialect, which was really extremely unpleasant to hear. Our young aunt was a woman who was good at teasing and playing pranks, so she often tried to imitate him with a curled tongue, saying, "La kuai, zhe kuai, aiyo kuai!"

"Ah Chang, you are so stupid: you've been here for five or six years, and you still can't get rid of your Jiangbei accent." My mother sometimes said to him when he couldn't understand "La kuai? Zhe kuai?" She would say this angrily, but he would just grin, showing his teeth, and reply, "I can't learn this kuai stuff." And that was that.

After my father died, our family's financial situation deteriorated day by day. Therefore, we had to try our best to economize on daily expenses, and that extra person was also dismissed.

"Madam! I have nowhere to go, please save me!" When my mother settled his wages and was about to ask him to leave, he knelt on the ground, kowtowing and begging my mother. My mother was moved by compassion, so she finally kept him for another half a year. After half a year, my mother introduced him to a local gentleman's family as a sedan chair carrier.

Ah Chang's savings over the years had surprisingly reached more than three hundred dollars. The year before last, he asked my mother to help him marry a maid from a wealthy family in Huzhou. This year, when I returned to my hometown, his child was already babbling.

Unequal Distribution! 198

Little Western Paradise 199

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Ten: Ashamed of Having No Clothes, He Avoids Guests Behind Curtains; Diligently Saving Lamp Oil, He Copies Books at Dawn

Zhiqian said, "I don't know about that. But judging from how everyone is saving lamp oil, it's obvious that the students provide their own light. Think about it, they don't even prepare vegetables for their meals; would they be willing to spend more money to buy lamp oil? They don't buy oil, and the school doesn't buy oil either. As a result, everyone has to sit in the dark. Once it gets dark, the time is wasted, and they feel it's a pity. So they adapt to the circumstances and go to bed early and get up to work as soon as it gets light. Wang Beihai listened from the side without saying a word. Now that Zhiqian had finished speaking, he couldn't help but interrupt, smiling, 'Mr. Cheng says that the students in the interior are suffering. Of course, that's true for students in Xi'an and above. But eating hard cornbread and drinking millet soup without vegetables might not be suffering.' Zhiqian slapped his thigh and laughed, 'Ah! I forgot you were like that too. But students like you are only a part of the students in Xi'an, but the whole student body is the same in the school I am talking about. Furthermore, you probably didn't have the pain of not having light when you want to read through the night. So, I felt endless emotion after I visited that elementary school. People engaged in education should go to the grassroots instead of sitting in big cities, talking about education theory, and thinking about education plans. What's the use? It's like the elementary school I mentioned, there are too many problems. How can we stop them from copying books? How can we prevent them from sleeping when it gets dark and getting up to copy books when it gets light? This is the first step in implementing education. But I think the education administrators wouldn't dream that there is such a phenomenon in county-run elementary schools in county towns, right?' (198)"

Records of the Fragrant Imperial Aroma 200

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Dear readers, imagine how trivial everything we have discussed above is. Inside the Summer Palace, just like a beehive, so many special industrial workshops were clustered together, and they were all similarly trivial and busy. Every artisan was constantly working hard, but the original driving force behind their hard work was simply the Empress Dowager's occasional happiness: Her old self only had to think of an idea, and that would be enough to keep these artisans busy! Although they, like all of them, received preferential treatment far beyond what ordinary workers could dream of, they could not have any say in their work, so it would not be wrong to call them a group of male and female prisoners.

However, in fact, most of the male and female artisans looked like very comfortable and happy prisoners who voluntarily lived in this prison indefinitely.

After they worked so hard for a few years or decades, it was rare to happen by chance that one person's work was loved by the Empress Dowager, and she praised them in front of everyone: this person would be so happy that they would even forget their own birth date, and the rest of the people would be inspired by this and work even harder. But how could the Empress Dowager praise them casually? Who knows how long it would take for such a rare event to happen!

Every time the Empress Dowager talked to me about these industries in the palace, she always had a long speech, either planning how to add new products or planning how to train new artisans, and her words were always detailed and practical: therefore, I often secretly admired her, believing that if her old self were hired to manage a factory, she would definitely be a very capable leader. What was particularly surprising about her innate talent was her memory: she often remembered many very small things very clearly, even though the artisans who were directly involved had forgotten them; therefore, no matter what kind of craftsmanship it was, the position of supervisor had to be taken by the Empress Dowager herself. (308)"

Small Gathering in Late Spring of Yi Hai, Briefly Sent to Ji Ping 201

— Yang An

The small gathering has no host or guest, voices responding to each other, dangerous words alarming the world, wild manner despising princes and dukes. Eloquent words are always short, lingering thoughts are always abundant, scholars are only true to themselves, why should they ever bow their heads?

Rare to gather with good friends, sweeping away ten thousand *hu* of dust, witty remarks enlivening all around, unrestrained joy competing with the spring. Shared heart for saving the country, unique care for becoming a better person, a single cup can reminisce about the past, don't just be an idle body!

Following Mr. Yang Yao's Rhyme 202

— Ji Ping

We struggle amidst baldness, unable to seek wealth and fame, always possessing the riches of a hundred cities, why need the status of ten thousand households? Happily pursuing peach and plum banquets, intending to be as carefree as clouds and water, I sit on the stone of Master Sheng, nodding with a flushed face.

The north wind rises overnight, covering the dust of the Tartars at the end of the sky, grass grows in the summer south of the Yangtze River, flowers wither in the spring north of the border. Tears remain beside the wine cup, the horn of a snail mistakes relatives for enemies, how much joy is in drunkenness, sharing these hundred feelings.

World News

— (Bing Yu)

A Precious Ring

Mrs. Leiluo Di Kai Li of the United States recently received a precious ring from the Egyptian era. This ring was originally in the coffin of an Egyptian king. It was cast in gold and silver and has colors such as red, green, and blue. It has a gold mummy image and a lover's image. There is a lid on the outside. According to archaeologists' speculation, this ring is two thousand years old and is a priceless treasure.

Highest Record for Hunger Strike

Mahatma Gandhi of India once went on a hunger strike for twenty-one days for the nation. However, the Irish patriot Terence MacSwiney, the former mayor of Cork, was arrested by the British authorities and imprisoned in a London prison for supporting the independence movement. However, he was unyielding and refused to eat. He went on a hunger strike for seventy-one days, and died of starvation on the seventy-fifth day. The second was the Indian patriot Jatindra Nath Das, who also died in prison after a hunger strike of sixty-one days. The third was the Egyptian patriot Tayhef Shen, who died after a hunger strike of fifty days.

Forcing the Old and Young to Smoke

In the area of the Danube River in eastern Serbia, fierce poisonous snakes are rampant, and there are reports of residents being harmed every day. Later, it was discovered that poisonous snake bites can be detoxified by spraying tobacco smoke. Therefore, the Serbian government issued a smoking order, requiring men, women, old and young, to smoke, and ordered teachers in elementary schools to guide them on how to smoke. Therefore, people in that area have cigarettes and cigars in their mouths, and smoke is everywhere, and people cannot be seen across the street. In particular, women regard smoking as the most fashionable, and compete to be novel.

The Largest Airplane

The Rong Jia Si Ge large airplane made in Germany in the past can carry twenty-four people, and it was the largest airplane in the world. This time, Russia has newly made a plane that can carry seventy-six people. It is also equipped with wireless telecommunications and a photography and printing room. The left and right wings are six meters long, equipped with eight engines with four thousand horsepower. It can fly two hundred and forty kilos every hour. It is scheduled to be completed by the end of this year.

A Strange Diary

Western America was originally inhabited by Indian tribes. A handwritten diary was unearthed in that mine. On the 25th of last month, Mr. Qiu Jia, who lives on 57th Street in New York, sold the first photographic edition at the Lita Huo Bosen Gallery for a high price of four hundred and eighty yuan. According to this diary, which was written by Sa Meng Teer, he started from the Lie Xiu Fei Er in the state of Illinois, broke through many mountains and rivers, and went all the way to the Sacramento Valley. The situation he experienced was recorded in detail in this diary.

Animals from 100,000 Years Ago

The National Museum in Washington, D.C., preserves a dinosaur skeleton that is 95 million years old. It is about fifteen feet tall and weighs about two tons. Steel rods are now used to support various parts of the skeleton, maintaining its original shape.

A Dog that Can Hatch Ostriches

John Bobby of Los Angeles, California, has a pet dog that is very intelligent and knows what people want. Last month, John bought ostrich eggs and ordered the dog to incubate them. In less than a week, the eggs hatched.

US Cotton Faces Selling Pressure at 12 Cents - Market Showed a Reactionary Trend Last Week 211

A New York dispatch on the cotton market for the week reports that the cotton market showed a reactionary trend last week. Due to the scarcity of spot goods and firmness in other commodity prices, selling pressure emerged as cotton prices approached 12 cents. Revised estimates for Indian cotton production have also increased, so there are concerns about competition from foreign cotton. Inquiries for spot exports are sluggish, and local users are unwilling to buy, due to factory production cuts, firm cotton prices, and weak spot sales.

Grains: Prospects of Rain Strengthen Both Flour and Wheat 213

The flour market opened strongly this morning, with consistent gains across all months. Overseas wheat was quoted, with Chicago down 0.30 and Canada down approximately 0.08. Initial pricing for overseas wheat was low, and market sentiment was calm. However, due to cloudy weather and the summer festival, as well as slight transactions in spot flour by northern merchants, subsequent prices improved. Although market sentiment was good, trading was light, as the new wheat harvest is approaching, and only those with urgent needs were active, otherwise both insiders and outsiders are adopting a wait-and-see approach. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading remained sluggish, but selling was scarce and buying was strong, leading to a price increase of about 0.01. Given these circumstances, the weather is the key factor in price fluctuations, making predictions difficult. As a result, the current month rose by 0.0225, June-July rose by 0.0225, August rose by 0.0175, September rose by 0.0225, and October rose by 0.01.

The wheat market opened largely steady this morning, with overseas wheat quoted down approximately 0.30 in Chicago and approximately 0.08 in Canada. Initial pricing was affected by cloudy weather and prospects of rain. With the new harvest approaching, rain would have a significant impact. Reports on wheat harvests varied across regions, with no definitive picture. With few sellers, the market gradually stabilized. In the afternoon, trading was relatively active, and sentiment remained positive. Due to cloudy weather and the rise in flour prices, prices also rose.
