Early rice rose by 0.10-0.20, and white yuan rice also closely followed, rising by several cents. Other varieties also showed a tightening trend.

The prospect for foreign rice continues to improve. However, yesterday, as rice merchants continued to purchase broken rice and lower-quality rice, sales to the Yangtze River and northern merchants slowed down. Local sales were also only slightly transactional. Only merchants from inland areas continued to actively purchase. As yesterday was the summer festival, some inland merchants did not arrive, and transactions decreased. As a result, the market turned from active to stable, and the upward trend slowed down. The total volume of various kinds of rice traded throughout the day was about 18,000 packages, with over 700 packages of Ke-Hsien rice. Prices were similar to those of the previous day.

Soybean Sales Sluggish, Weak Upward Momentum 215

Yesterday's soybean market was not much different from last Saturday. Factory demand was not strong, and sales were not active. However, traders in the local market were relatively relaxed on pricing. Given the lack of large-scale purchases, the upward momentum is likely to be weak. The total market volume included one truckload of Quanhe beans, priced at 3.78; one truckload of Yingzhou beans, priced at 3.65; one truckload of Haozhou beans, priced at 3.55-3.65; over 410 packages of Luohe beans, priced at 3.81; one truckload of Huangkou beans, priced at 3.68; one truckload of Xikou beans, priced at 3.56; over 1,000 packages of Hankou early beans, priced from 3.95 to 3.75; and 43 packages of Hankou late beans, priced at 3.62.

Sugar Market: Continued Arrivals of Dutch Sugar, 23,476 Packages 216

Yesterday's sugar market trend was relatively stable, with a slightly tight tone. The public association quoted 16.04 for Dutch granulated sugar 24, and foreign warehouse goods were quoted at 5.20, a 0.05 increase for transit goods. There were no transactions. Taikoo Sugar B mark was quoted at 17.02. Local factory cotton white Zhenyu No. 1 was quoted at 15.085, No. 2 at 15.075, No. 3 at 15.06, and No. 4 at 15.045, unchanged from the previous day. Local ice sugar No. 1 was quoted at 21.06, and No. 2 at 21.5. Chaoqing sugar remained firm and had not been traded, with few sales.

The Dutch steamship Djassar had imported from Surabaya, arriving with 502 packages of Dutch red sugar, 4,259 packages of refined granulated sugar, and 25 packages of raw granulated sugar. The Dutch steamship Djassar Deni also arrived with 502 packages of Dutch red sugar, 27,963 packages of coarse granulated sugar, totaling 33,476 packages.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Breaks Through 40 Yuan Again 218

The price of white tung oil in Hankou's foreign firms has risen again. After rising from 35-36 yuan to 39 yuan last week, the situation has become increasingly tight. As this week began, there were signs of a storm brewing. Last night, local firms received telegrams from Hankou stating that foreign firms had sold at 40.05 yuan for spot goods. As such, the market price is likely to break through 40 yuan. And the momentum is still strong, so another 1-2 yuan increase is possible. However, if it rises to 42-43 yuan, it can be considered as reaching its peak. Although it may not immediately fall back, it may stabilize. Due to the high prices for exports, foreign firms may find it difficult to make a profit. Once foreign firms stop purchasing, the market will weaken. Even if there is an attempt to maintain it, it cannot last long. As domestic sales are too light, the key to price fluctuations lies entirely in the strength of exports. Therefore, oil firms in Hankou have no confidence in the market and are simply following the market. Although there are some transactions with foreign firms in this city, the volume is very small. The production volume of Zhejiang tung oil is limited and cannot supply large quantities. The local market cannot stand independently from the Hankou market. Even if there are transactions, they cannot be considered standard.

Free Talk

Psychological Depiction in Works 220

— Qu Yi

Psychological depiction in works, in terms of its techniques, roughly has three styles. First, before and after writing a character, the author provides an explanatory-style description. Second, when depicting a character, the author narrates their actions and reflects their psychology along the way. Third, the author objectively portrays a character, making them stand before the reader naturally. The author does not focus on psychological depiction, but the character's psychology is clearly understood by the reader. It is not difficult to find examples to illustrate these three styles. However, in this short article, we can only touch on the topic and cannot quote large excerpts from current writers' works as evidence.

Generally, the first technique is not often seen in new writers' works. It is the laziest and oldest technique. The author of "The Laughing and Crying Marriage," in their daily life of writing five or six thousand words, specifically used this technique to lengthen the story. Therefore, this technique sometimes becomes a burden to the article.

The second technique is the most innovative. In this type of depiction, the entire piece shows only the character's movements, and the author's face is never revealed in the piece. Mr. Zhang Tianyi is very skilled and clever in using this technique. His "Bees," "Determinism," and "Fortune Telling" are the best examples.

Although the third technique has existed since ancient times, the author of "Hesitation" and "Call to Arms" can be considered as using it appropriately. Many of the typical characters in the two collections of novels, "Hesitation" and "Call to Arms," are vividly portrayed, each with its own characteristics. The author does not intend to depict psychology, but in practice, penetrates into the realm of psychological depiction. In this technique, the author does not adhere to explaining the character's psychology, but can create a contrast or reflection in the relationship between characters. There is a passage in "Dream of the Red Chamber" where Jia Rong borrows a glass pit screen from Wang Xifeng, which is a very good psychological depiction. After Jia Rong had already borrowed the screen, "Wang Xifeng thought of another matter. She called out to the window: 'Rong'er, come back!' Several people outside echoed: 'Master Rong, come back quickly'… He stood by with his hands hanging down, listening to her instructions. Wang Xifeng slowly drank her tea, and after a long time, she smiled and said: 'Alright, you can go now.'… This can be said to vividly depict Wang Xifeng's joy for Jia Rong.

However, these two psychological depiction techniques are determined by each writer's creative methods. Generally, the first type of author is mostly based on a philosophy of idealism, wanting to understand social psychology through the dissection of individual psychology in literature. The second type of author does not necessarily recognize the social relations of the characters in the work, but often simplifies the characters' social relations. As a result, the character's personality is expressed very actively, but obscures the foundation of the personality's development. Undoubtedly, the author starts from a realistic perspective and then goes down the psychological path. Only the third type of author has a correct social view. Although the characters in their book are used as examples, rather than focusing on individuality. Although "their value lies not in being different from other characters in the same situation, but in being the same, that is, in their commonality, not in their characteristics." But "examples" must also have "typicality," and "commonality" must also be clearly contrasted with another "commonality" to show their characteristics. Only in this way can the characters in the work be expressed more realistically and have more life.

Unexpected Events 221

— Qin Wen

Because of the severe noise from mosquitoes and rats, I didn't fall asleep until the latter half of the night, and I still didn't wake up at dawn, and I started dreaming. Dreaming is common, but it's rare to have such a wonderful dream and feel so comforted. To suddenly have such a dream, something I hadn't thought of before, was also unexpected, because the person I was playing with in the dream was someone I had only recently met.

Dreaming is indeed common; dreaming well, sometimes even expecting it, isn't strange. Similarly, being startled awake from a dream is also common, and a good dream is naturally often interrupted. But this time, I suddenly had a very rare dream, and just as I was having fun playing, the sweet feeling was suddenly interrupted, shaken awake by an earthquake.

I live on one side of the Taiwan Strait, so for more than two months since spring, I have been frequently attacked by strong winds and heavy rains. This time, the earthquake in Taiwan, with its aftershocks, shook my bed and windows, which isn't really that strange. But how can it be such a coincidence: that I happened to be drifting here to live at this time, met such a person, had such a gathering in a dream, and was awakened in this way?

The bed and window lattice creaked three times in a row, and then again after more than twenty minutes; I couldn't sleep anymore, so I started thinking randomly, and the more I thought, the more inexplicable it seemed. When I think about it, in these past few years, many of the things encountered, both for the country and for individuals, have been unexpected.

I also remembered such an unexpected event; the spring before last, I went to Mount Emei to travel, walking from Jin Ding to Wanfo Ding, and on one side of Qianfo Ding, I saw a young man wandering on the road, in his twenties, wearing tattered clothes and short trousers. Not a monk, nor a pilgrim, and judging by his thin appearance, not a "porter" either. To encounter such a person on this high mountain was already unexpected. But he came up to me as soon as he saw me and asked:

"Sir! Can I be a monk here?"

This was even more unexpected, and I really couldn't deal with it for a moment. But things became even more unexpected, and before I could answer, his face tightened, and he began to cry softly; tears dripped down, falling one after another onto the sandy soil in front of his feet. I asked why, but he couldn't even speak.

Upon closer examination, this cannot be considered so strange. At that time in Sichuan, people were often being killed with machetes in the streets, and those being killed were deserters; these "soldiers" were "recruited," so they often tried to escape. Also, because of the heavy taxes, some people were forced to abandon their property and leave their hometowns. Although it cannot be said for sure that this young man was a fugitive, it can be asserted that he was forced up Mount Emei by the hardships of life. There are indeed many, many people living poorly, so it is not really strange. But at the time, I always felt it was unexpected.

Waiting Room 222

— Yang Cheng

The waiting room of the women and children's hospital is filled with the cries of children.

Mothers sit on long benches. Older children walk around. Babies are gurgling and learning to talk, sometimes unknowingly urinating in their mothers' arms, leaving a wet pattern on the qipao that the mothers only wear when going out.

A woman in ragged clothes walked in. Her whole body covered in snow, her eyelids tiredly staring, flickering with red veins; she held a dried-up infant close, the child's head covered in small, uneven sores, two streams of snot hanging down from the corners of its mouth. It gnawed haphazardly on a cornbread bun.

Her surprised gaze constantly darted around this unfamiliar place, she wanted to sit on a bench with the other mothers, but she didn't dare; she could only huddle alone in the corner against the wall, squatting down on the floor.

A nurse in white walked up to her, first covering her nose, then saying harshly:

"Isn't that place not for sitting? Humph, what are you doing squatting like that?" Pointing to the bench, "Sir—oh, Miss." Her widened, lifeless eyes filled with gratitude, yet also with a bitter smile.

People had already started snickering. As soon as she sat on the bench, the ladies nearby covered their noses and walked away, deliberately spitting.

By half-past eleven, only a few scattered people remained in the room, and she was finally noticed, then called in. A doctor, as thin as a consumptive child, slowly spoke after examining the child:

"Don't give the child cornbread buns indiscriminately, wash the sores on the head with medicinal water every day, and for a fever, it's best to drink some milk, um, milk... Now, get the medicine." And he gave her a slip of paper.

"Three times a day, two dollars." The pharmacist handed over the blue-red medicinal water.

At first, she listened blankly, but the last sentence seemed to sting her, and she blurted out:

"How much? Miss."

"Two dollars. " The person spoke with a nasal tone. "I don't have that much money, I scraped together the three dimes for the registration fee over several days. Please, have some compassion, give me back my three dimes, I don't want the medicine."

"That's not my problem, you have to ask at the registration desk." She lowered her head, looked at her watch, it was exactly twelve o'clock, and slammed the dispensing window shut.

She went out the door, feeling very suffocated, the child wasn't cured; and she lost three dimes for nothing. She regretted coming to this foreign hospital, she couldn't stand the foreignness of it all.

Outside, the snow was still falling, she walked step by step down the white street. A thought crossed her mind: she should find a general practitioner instead. Thinking this, her pace quickened.

Mourning Lost Friendship 223

— Chi Xia

There was a time when I lost a friend's heart. I had taken warmth from it, received sympathy, and easily lost it over a small matter. At the time, I didn't feel sad, but the desolation of time brought back memories of the past, gradually making me feel regret, a nameless emptiness, mixed with boundless sorrow, suddenly floating up from the bottom of my heart.

It's been two years since I've seen this friend. In these two years, I've been living in a crowd, like traveling in a desert. From afar, a heart left me and went away, and I seemed to have no power to pull it back. My soul slowly became withered. I abandoned all friends, cutting them off by isolation. All friends also abandoned me, scorning me with contempt. I only felt lonely. How precious is a friend's heart! If a woman is considered a pearl of solace in life, then a true friend can be compared to a steadfast diamond. Unfortunately, this steadfast diamond slipped through my fingers. For two years, I've felt like I've lost my center of gravity, my soul constantly floating in a haze.

Those who have read Anatole France's "Lettre de mon ami" can understand the preciousness of friendship. "On the journey of life, a friend is your only comforter," "A woman can only moisten your soul, but cannot fill it. A friend gives you the greatest assistance in the latter's demands." In those days, I didn't understand the true meaning of these words. Now, I understand the profound meaning. True friendship can make your life move upward. In times of difficulty, it gives you assistance without seeking reward. In times of disappointment, it drips out its own life force to encourage you to move forward again. Unexpectedly, you will receive letters from him from afar. Every sentence on the long paper can be read as being very concerned. Whether under flowers or before a lamp, his shadow flickers around you, thus causing a feeling of comfort, making you feel that everything around you is very lovely, and that the future is filled with great hope. Even when you fail in your career, you can muster the strength that hasn't died to reclaim everything that has been lost.

When such an emotional force leaves my side, as the days go by, one naturally feels an unspeakable emptiness. The hearts of two people become more and more distant, even more isolated than strangers. I thought about pulling him back, but in the end, I didn't have the strength to do it. The days passed in hesitation, and the friendship of the past flowed away like passing water and never returned.

The past, like smoke, is woven into my heart at this moment. Things change too quickly. Two years ago today, I never dreamed that I would lose the heart of this friend!

A Corner of a Carriage 224

— TK

Three Days (4) 225

— Luo Hong

Just like himself, his father died when he was twenty-three. At that time, his younger brother, Youcai, was still young and couldn't do much. He worked hard alone for seven or eight years, paying off the debts left by his father and arranging Youcai's marriage. Although he didn't clear all the old debts, he managed to patch things up year after year, so at least new debts didn't accumulate. However, life was indeed getting harder and harder. Even going to town to buy something was getting more expensive every year. According to Hu Yongliang and the others, it was the rich people causing trouble in the middle. He really didn't understand how they came up with these ideas. What did these things have to do with rich people? The year there was a famine, not a single grain of rice could be harvested from the fields. Even though he reported the famine to the granary and didn't have to repay the rent rice, he still needed rice to eat and capital for next year's farming. Fortunately, Master Lu discussed it with several yamen runners in the county and set up this loan society. Everyone could borrow from it, with only a small amount of interest. When borrowing, one-tenth of the principal was deducted first. For example, if you borrowed one hundred, ten yuan was deducted first. When the principal and interest were repaid in full next year, this deducted amount would be removed from the interest. However, everyone had to hand over guarantee rice first. If you planted five mu, you would measure out one dou per mu and deposit it in this loan society. If a household had more than ten mu, they would have to measure out five dou per mu. Once the rice ripened in the fields, regardless of the harvest, this guarantee rice had to be handed over first. The money borrowed from the loan society also had to be repaid in full when the rice ripened, otherwise, you couldn't borrow again next time. But in this village, hardly one in ten families didn't rely on this loan society. As soon as the rice ripened, they would first repay the borrowed debts, and then borrow again at the end of the year. If it weren't for these masters taking pity and doing good deeds, they wouldn't be able to get through the years.

Youfa sighed heavily and raised his right hand to touch his brush-like beard. He didn't understand how people who were only ten years younger than him had become so strange. His younger brother had always been diligent and hardworking, and he didn't talk much. He wasn't involved in anything in the village, but unexpectedly, after Hu Yongliang whispered something, he had become that annoying.

But how could he reply to Master Lu? If he said that Youcai's wife couldn't be a wet nurse, then the two hundred dollars couldn't be borrowed no matter what. If he dared to agree, then Youcai would be stubborn, and it seemed he definitely wouldn't agree.

The child's crying burst out from the kitchen again, the sound was very loud, as if it was a little angry. This crying interrupted Youfa's thoughts. He looked at the sky, the rain had lessened a bit, but the lead-like sky was still heavily pressing down on the ground, and it didn't seem like it would clear up for three or five days. So he resented the sky again. If it had rained a few days later, after they had harvested the rice and threshed the grain, then when there was really no other way, they could mortgage some of the grain for money, which might be hopeful. But now they had only harvested a little more than one mu of rice, what use was that!

At the same time, Master Lu puffed up his sparse ten beard hairs and also sighed heavily. But the sound wasn't as heavy as Youfa's. Although it was drawn out so long, it couldn't hide the proud and complacent look on his face.

"Master, don't worry so much, I'll definitely think of a way for you." Huang Zhongpu, sitting diagonally across from Master Lu, revealed a mouthful of yellow teeth, his face full of smiles, following Master Lu's sigh.

Master Lu didn't seem to hear. He only stared at the cigarette holder in his right hand. The ivory mouthpiece was newly bought from the city, half a foot long, said to be the most fashionable item. Although Master Lu didn't approve of newfangled things, he really approved of this cigarette holder. It was much better than a water pipe, more convenient, and more beautiful. He looked at the cigarette holder in a daze, only a fraction of his expression seemed like sighing, while seven fractions were admiring the ivory mouthpiece.

Huang Zhongpu's smile receded by half, and the yellow teeth were exposed outside for more than a minute, but Master Lu didn't show any movement, so he closed his lips, moistened his row of yellow teeth with his tongue, and said with a smile again:

"Master, don't worry, getting a Ningxin is worth a little trouble. Changing wet nurses, you, the Lu family, just have to say you want a wet nurse, and who wouldn't want to come? Let Master be picky."

Master Lu's eyes finally left the ivory mouthpiece, and he gently flicked the mouthpiece with his index finger, the fingernail making an extremely crisp sound against the ivory, and a pile of ashes floated to the ground. Then he took two heavy puffs, and while puffing out smoke, he said:

"But I want things done as quickly as possible. Didn't you say that Youcai's wife's milk is very good? Then definitely have her come try first."

"But... but that money,"

"That money, I'll only be willing to lend it once they agree. I want my wet nurse, I'm not afraid of not having anyone. If they don't agree, let them borrow from someone else."

Master Lu spoke the last sentence with particular emphasis. He understood very well that if Youfa and the others wanted to borrow money at this time, there was no one else but him, Master Lu.

Supplement to Shenbao Local News

Random Thoughts

The Orchestra's Hybrid Incongruity 226

— Chen

The result of "Chinese learning as the fundamental structure, Western learning for practical application" has been to add a lot of power to our "Eastern civilization." On a grand scale, things like guns and electric chairs have greatly improved the technology of killing and torture. On a small scale, things like radios and gramophones have expanded the scope of "Yangzhou tunes," "Wuxi scenery," and even "Namo Amitabha," making them "popular." In between, after the shouts of "Avoidance" and "Silence," a "Red-Headed Sikh" cavalry patrol is deployed, and before the "four-person sedan chair," a weak military band performs. In this "international city" and other large cities, we often display the wonderful scene of bringing together ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign.

The phenomenon itself is, in fact, already bizarre and incongruous. However, from famous officials and wealthy merchants to ordinary citizens, whenever there is a "white or red auspicious occasion," they all regard it as a necessary "grand display." It seems that not doing so is not enough to express "mourning" or "celebration," but in fact, it is not enough to express "ostentation." The result of "ostentation" is a lot of jokes, especially in this "ten-mile foreign concession" where "Chinese and foreigners are watching," it is really "damaging to the national image." Therefore, the authorities have taken measures to ban it, and in terms of "manifesting solemnity and encouraging good customs," it is indeed a pleasing and welcome measure.

I think that many lucky people in China, if they have a national character, would not sacrifice a hair to benefit the world. If they have no national character, they will do everything they can to indulge in the ostentatious and exaggerated rituals of "aristocratic families." The banners of a certain "hall" that we see in Shanghai for "weddings, funerals, and sacrifices" are often even greater and more magnificent than the police force in an anti-enemy expedition. As this trend spreads, cavalry patrols, Red-Headed Sikhs, theatrical stages, trumpets, monks, Taoists, firecrackers, military bands, and all kinds of musical instruments and the nine streams of society are pulled together. Thus, the wooden signs of "Avoidance" and "Silence" cause ordinary citizens to rub shoulders and the roads to be blocked. This kind of thing is really no different from a "thousands-of-years-old, tens-of-thousands-of-miles" antique exhibition.

So, if it is said that the orchestra's playing of popular tunes at funerals and mournful music at wedding banquets is "unseemly," then putting so many different and varied things together is not necessarily able to "manifest solemnity and encourage good customs"!

Night Crossing 227

— Yuan Zhi

A group of five people, all driven by a kind of curiosity, a beautiful imagination, and a long-held yearning, bravely embarked on the country road at night, regardless of everything.

It was around the tenth day of the lunar month, and the waxing crescent moon hung diagonally in a corner of the sky. The countryside was bathed in silver light, but the scenery in the distance was hazy and indistinct.

The five people walked at a not-so-fast pace, lightly floating in the sea of moonlight as if swimming. The narrow field path was bordered by boundless wheat fields. The heavily laden wheat stalks leaned towards the road, and the ears and leaves of wheat often brushed against the lower clothes and socks of the night travelers.

However, they paid no attention to these, but concentrated their attention on one focal point, which was how to make this short trip more interesting and meaningful. Everyone was talking and laughing enthusiastically. Some were even smoking cigarettes, and the gray-white smoke curled up into the air, slowly thinning and disappearing.

The three-mile-long country road slipped under the excited feet of the several people, as if they didn't even notice. It wasn't until they heard the dogs barking wildly in Maohutou Village ahead that everyone seemed to wake up from a dream and realize that they had reached the lake.

The people in the village were not asleep yet, and some were still eating dinner. Many people noticed these five strange young men, and quickly surrounded them. But the villagers had no malice at all, just surprise. When the young men explained that they wanted to hire a boat to cross the lake, several boatmen scrambled to solicit business.

The young men decided to hire that person's boat and followed him to the lake (which was actually only fifty or sixty feet away in front of the village). In order, they each stepped onto the "gangplank" and crawled into the cabin. The boatman also boarded the boat, making a total of two people; one punted at the bow and the other rowed at the stern. With everything arranged, the boat skillfully sailed towards the dark Mount Fujiao in the middle of the lake.

The boat was specially used for crossing the lake, so it was called a "lake-crossing boat." It was different from those boats that navigate the inland rivers; it had two extra wings. That is, there were two planks on both sides of the boat, dragged in the water. In this way, you didn't have to worry about the lake waves being frantic, and you could sail safely.

"Mate, how long does it take to cross the lake?"

"Today, the wind is favorable, and the waves are not big. In the time it takes to smoke two cigarettes, you can definitely reach Mount Fujiao." The boatmen didn't have watches. They didn't know exactly how many minutes it would take to reach the other shore, but they used cigarettes to test it, and experience made their answers very confident.

The young men already knew that the lake was ten miles wide, but they didn't expect that it would only take the time to smoke two cigarettes to cross. This was new knowledge for them. Because of this, everyone was even happier and felt that the trip was more valuable. Therefore, although the boat was swaying slightly there, and the lake waves were constantly slapping against the hull and making splashing sounds, they didn't care at all and didn't feel the slightest fear.

The moon was dragged behind the boat, illuminating the surface of the waves, and was constantly smashed to pieces by the oars. Every ray of moonlight shot on the bulging wave crest, just like the back of every glistening water snake, forever chasing the boat and swimming forward.

The lake at night was empty and vast, and its borders were indistinct and boundless. There was only this one boat sailing, which made it seem even more lonely and serene. However, the hearts of the young men were hot, and they hoped for the arrival of the other shore; everyone's eyes were fixed on the cigarette butt of a young man who was calculating the distance.

When the second cigarette had been smoked for the most part, the boatman shouted that Mount Fujiao had arrived. The young men paid a generous boat fare and jumped ashore one by one. Everyone's heart was filled with new excitement and new charm.

Fog 228

— Xia Yin

For several days, the misty, foggy weather has been truly annoying. When there is no fog, the clear sky in the morning, the fields under the bright sun, and the sunset over the willow forest in this corner of the small building are all like a close-up shot, unfolding in a picturesque way in the east and west windows. Although I am not a poet or a painter, and cannot think of a beautiful poem in this scenery, or paint a picture, I can indeed feel a comfortable intoxication and a fresh and beautiful satisfaction from the silent prospect. Rather than saying that this is leisure and idle pleasure, it is more appropriate to say that the tired body and mind, especially for the gentle and relaxed environment, need and feel more deeply the state of things. Therefore, the melancholy that the dense fog has given me in these past few days has been particularly turbid and dull, like suddenly covering my eyes with a white gauze, a hazy and turbid piece, unable to distinguish direction, height, width, or narrowness; even breathing has an unnatural feeling, as if isolated from the world. Therefore, I cannot help but hate the fog, even curse the fog, and feel infinite annoyance and discomfort in my heart.

People always love to have a bright world that can provide freedom, galloping, and activity. Although the fog does not yet hinder me or restrict my activities in human affairs, it does have an invisible and silent curse, blinding my heart and blurring my eyes, making me seem to be trapped in a turbid sea of ​​water and foam; just like an airplane or a ship in foggy weather, no matter how great its power, it cannot be freely exerted and used at this time. Although there are still fixed routes in the sky, rivers, and seas in the fog. Although the fog will not turn the universe into darkness, it will remove a mass of bottomless turbidity and obscurity from the universe.

I remember once at sea, when the ship encountered a thick fog, it was already dark night, the fog covered the sea densely, obscuring the light of the lighthouse, and all around was an endless darkness. The humid sea breeze, mixed with the cold of December, blew people shivering, and the sea waves beat against the hull, making angry sighs. Far away, the warning whistle of the lighthouse, passing through the foggy night sea, was drawn out, from high to weak, like an animal crying, eerily and indifferently radiating on the foggy night sea. The whistle on the ship also wailed, and then the frequent bell sounds rang intermittently, a kind of terrifying and tense air that made people suspect that the ship was in danger. In this way, I spent the night in the terrifying alarm whistle and the sound of chaotic bells until the fog cleared the next day and the ship set sail again. The terrifying impression that the fog gave me that time was so deep that every time I encountered a sea voyage, I would suspect that the fog would suddenly cover the sea, and I felt that the fog at sea was simply a cruel threat to the lives of seafarers.

Sympathizer 229

— Yu Yan

Second Uncle 230

— Hua Mu

Whenever I think of my maternal grandmother's house, I remember my second uncle, lying on the opium couch year after year, and my cousin, who was only eighteen and also addicted to opium. My mother would say with anger and sorrow:

—If it weren't for the sake of my elderly grandmother, I truly wouldn't want to step foot in the Zhang family's door again! Doesn't each visit only deepen my sorrow?

My grandmother's house wasn't exactly a scholarly family. Thanks to my maternal grandfather's lifelong diligence and thrift, he accumulated dozens of acres of land and a dyehouse of considerable size, making them a relatively prosperous family in the barren Changlin Village. Although my maternal grandfather came from a business background, he possessed a rare and admirable old-fashioned heart—a respected elder who fostered harmony among relatives and neighbors, earning him the villagers' respect and affection. In his later years, he lived in a two-story house with his children and grandchildren filling the halls, enjoying a life of comfort and ease.

However, this comfortable life was shattered two years before my maternal grandfather's death due to my second uncle's dissolute behavior and opium addiction, which caused him great sadness and anger. This also made my maternal grandfather think of his deceased eldest son, deepening the sorrow and pain in his heart. Before long, he breathed his last, passing away.

After becoming addicted to opium, my second uncle, fearing my maternal grandfather's authority, could only wander outside. Sometimes he would sneak back, but if my maternal grandfather found out, he would be driven out with his cane. During that time, my second uncle lived a very miserable life in opium dens. Later, when my maternal grandfather became critically ill, he was allowed to return. After my maternal grandfather's death, my second uncle seized control of the family, and the once well-to-do household began to decline under the suction of his opium pipe.

My maternal grandmother, accustomed to a life of leisure, only knew how to pray to Buddha and give alms. She was helpless against my second uncle's reckless spending. When her resentment became unbearable, she could only sigh and lament her misfortune in front of her daughters and daughters-in-law, complaining that she must have done something wrong in her past life to have given birth to such a troublesome son. Only my eldest aunt saw herself as my second uncle's nemesis, constantly nagging and scolding, scolding and then advising. However, when she discovered that her own son, my cousin, had also become addicted to opium, my eldest aunt, who was usually meticulous, concerned with appearances, extravagant, and fiercely competitive, was driven mad.

With my eldest aunt falling ill, my maternal grandmother became even more worried. But this made things much quieter for my second uncle. Even though the house was in constant turmoil, my second uncle, lying on his opium couch, felt at ease, contentedly indulging in his opium habit. With glazed eyes, he would drift into a dreamlike state, mentally planning his next moves while surrounded by the land deeds buried in the wooden pillow chest. My second uncle's opium addiction was truly terrifying. He consumed at least two ounces of opium paste day and night. Like a ghost, he lay there in the dim light of a small oil lamp. Except for eating, relieving himself, and taking the deeds out to find clients, he never took a single step out of his room.

One year, then two years passed. The land was gone, and the dyehouse had changed owners. By the third year—the third year after my maternal grandfather's death—although my eldest aunt's health was gradually improving, my second uncle began to worry about his opium supply, and my maternal grandmother, due to her repressed grief, developed an incurable wasting disease.

Soon, the opium lamp and smoking paraphernalia on my second uncle's couch ended up in the opium den as collateral. My second uncle returned to the miserable life he had led when he was driven out by my maternal grandfather. Once, my second uncle, dragging his broken shoes, came to our door with his head lowered in dejection. He begged my mother for a few coins, saying that he hadn't had a haircut in three months. However, my mother refused. Afterwards, I said that my mother was being too harsh, and her eyes reddened as she said:

—How could I not be heartbroken? But I had told him long ago that this day would come. I don't even have the ability to provide for my grandmother, how can I possibly take care of him! If your grandfather were still alive, I wouldn't be so… My mother's voice choked, and a shadow of sorrow passed before my eyes. I understood my mother's bitter heart.

My Humble Abode 231

— Ji Huan

When I happened to meet Mr. Zi Qiu on the street, as usual, he would begin the conversation with a forced smile and a phrase like, "The weather is fine today." So I took a closer look at Mr. Zi Qiu: still his withered limbs, and the large, shapeless robe that seemed to be draped over him; still his sharp shoulders; still his haggard face; still his eyes that seemed perpetually unfocused from lack of sleep; still that faded and frayed felt hat; still that demeanor of being intimidated by the harshness of reality, having fallen from the pinnacle of life and being seriously injured, burrowing into a dead end of self-pity, and trying to use alcohol and excessive sleep as a refuge, resulting in a muddled mind; still a string of stuttering words that seemed to betray his anxiety, confusion, and shyness due to his inability to express himself adequately: "You, you… have you been doing well lately—doing well? I, I, I—your brother has been, has been—please come to my humble abode sometime, please come to my humble abode sometime to chat. I've moved, uh, moved…"

As if he had touched upon something unpleasant again, Mr. Zi Qiu, without waiting for a reply, hastily bowed and disappeared into the crowd in the bright sunlight.

The phrase "humble abode" once again struck my senses. These are only two simple syllables, but when spoken by Mr. Zi Qiu, they convey a sense of heaviness and suffocation. I seemed to see a snail slowly crawling along the base of a wall with its heavy shell; I seemed to taste the weight of a fallen mountain; I seemed to feel an infinitely heavy burden pressing down, forcing one to take heavy and difficult steps, step by step, towards the desolate wilderness of life, not knowing where the final resting place might be…

Mr. Zi Qiu already had a haggard face and unclear speech three years ago. At that time, I was living in a rented room in a pavilion in a southern metropolis; Mr. Zi Qiu was my neighbor, living upstairs in the main hall. He wasn't particularly old, but within his frighteningly thin frame, he always carried an unmistakable air of bitterness and sentimentality associated with the "broken shoe party." Even when arguing with the landlady about rent, he would try to embellish his arguments with quotations from the Thirteen Classics, but he often "couldn't remember them at the moment." In the end, he would simply mutter, "Only women and petty men are difficult to deal with!" This, to him, was as satisfying as Ah C's "Old man beating his son!"

So, there was always a quarrel at the end of each month, and after the quarrel, one could hear the woman's lamenting cries from the "humble abode"…

But finally, one day, as I was walking down the stairs, I met Mr. Zi Qiu. I nodded and greeted him as he bowed.

The second time I saw him while idly watching at the doorway, he insisted on dragging me to his "humble abode" upstairs in the main hall. This "humble abode" consisted of Mr. Zi Qiu himself, a wife with bound feet, a mother in her seventies, and various pieces of old furniture scattered around the room.

Then I listened to him talk about his family history, his father's lifetime as a candidate official who never got a real position, the changes in the world, the greatness of the Tongcheng School, the landlady's unreasonableness, and the difficulties of life… the burden of the "humble abode"…

"If it weren't for the few mouths to feed in this humble abode, I would have jumped into the Huangpu River long ago, following the Great Qing Emperor. Life is really hard now, it's difficult to survive with so many people."

What followed was a request to borrow some money to deal with the landlady: "You are… you probably don't care, but please, for the sake of the few mouths in this humble abode, please…"

I seemed to see a tragedy in the midst of this detestable vulgarity; but the decaying stench of a bygone era made me nauseous. In a surge of bitterness and annoyance, I didn't give him a reply and stood up and left.

But meeting Mr. Zi Qiu again now, I knew that the hunchbacked, foul-smelling "humble abode" was still alive and well; but Mr. Zi Qiu's appearance was definitely not as good as before…

Chatting About "Night Fragrance" 237

"Night Fragrance" is a brand-new tragedy written and directed by Cheng Bugao. Its content is tragic, telling the story of a flower girl (played by Hu Die). Every time the lights come on, she carries a flower basket to the entrance of dance halls, cafes, or bars to sell "Night Fragrance." She supports herself, but eventually cannot escape the influence of the extravagant society, becomes obsessed with vanity, and falls into a situation from which she cannot extricate herself. Although she tries her best to struggle, it is all in vain. In the process of depicting the ill-fated woman, we can also see the environment around her, the silhouette of this turbulent era, such as the bankruptcy of villages, the corruption of cities, the frequent foreign insults, the hard lives of the masses, and the panic of professions, which can be said to be sentimental and eventful, very tortuous.

"Night Fragrance" is just waiting for Hu Die to return to film the remaining scenes, and it can be completed successfully.

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

The Essentials of the Latest Medical Building Design (Part 2) 238

— Liu Ji Piao

E (X-Ray Department) The location must be dry and not damp. It must also have a place where patients can enter and exit conveniently. The scale can be small:

(1) Fluoroscopy Room - Combining the radiology room and treatment room into one. 2 - Diagnostic office. 3 - Darkroom. 4 - Waiting room. Larger scale includes: 1 - One or more radiology rooms. 2 - One or more fluoroscopy rooms. 3 - Diagnostic and office. 4 - Treatment room. 5 - Darkroom. 6 - Waiting room. 7 - Changing room. Generally, this is the case. However, the number of rooms must be determined based on economic conditions and needs.

The ceiling should not be lower than 10 (from the floor to the bottom of the beam). The inner wall must be covered with lead (for fluoroscopy rooms and radiology rooms). The doors of these two rooms should also be wrapped in lead. If there are sickrooms on the upper and lower floors, the floors and ceilings of these two rooms should also be covered with to prevent light.

f. (Anatomy Department) Must be located in the basement. Close to the elevator and in a place where patients cannot see it when entering and exiting.

g. (Pharmaceutical Department) The pharmacy, material room, and testing room should all have northern light.

h. (Staff Dormitory) Regardless of the size of the hospital, the problem of staff accommodation must be resolved. Because mental fatigue occurs after work, there should be adequate rest. Therefore, the dormitory location must be close to the hospital and provide recreational enjoyment. Therefore, a tennis court and outdoor sports facilities are essential. Doctors with families need residential-style houses, so the design should also take this issue into account.

Nurse Dormitory and School. It is better for the nurse dormitory to be independent. However, it must also be connected to the hospital by a corridor. Common rooms should accommodate two people. Bathrooms and toilets should be opened separately. But it must be accessible from the bedroom. And it must be available for four or five people. Each floor is equipped with a small kitchen and sewing room. Public living rooms. Reception room. Gymnasium. Rain showers, etc. should also be set up as much as possible. There should be a gate near the street, and it is not necessary to pass through the hospital when entering. The nursing school can be located in the dormitory. But it can also be independent. The designer should make temporary arrangements based on his needs.

i. (Cooking Department) The cooking department must be located in a place that is convenient for entering and exiting and easy to supply goods. Set up another door so that it does not interfere with the hospital's business. But it must be close to the elevator, with a general kitchen inside. Kitchens that regulate diet. Dining rooms for nurses, supervisors. Workers and staff. Cooking management room.

j. (Boiler Room) The boiler room can be attached to the inside of the hospital or independent. Those attached to the inside must be close to the entrance and exit for supplying goods. If there is sufficient funding, it is best to set it in an independent location. This can make everything convenient.

k. (Laundry Room) It should be located in the basement, preferably under the children's ward. Because the children's spirits will not be disturbed by the washing work. However, the ceiling must also be constructed with soundproofing methods. If an independent location is taken, it is best to set it on the upper floor of the boiler room.

The above are just the essentials of each item. However, each hospital has its own conditions and needs. The designer should inspect the situation temporarily and determine the plan. The above points cannot be solved one by one. (End)

Architectural Jargon (11) 239

— Mei Zhen Huan

——Regarding use in construction sites——

Pump - In construction sites, the places flooded by accumulated water sometimes cause considerable harm to the work. Supervisors should always order small workers to pump dry with water-drawing equipment. This water-drawing equipment is called a pump. (Pump) Just like the sheet pile is called Waling, it is also taken from transliteration.

Knot - Foreign pine materials are divided into net goods and substandard goods. (That is, the meaning of first-class and second-class.) The quality of net goods is relatively sophisticated. It has been through a selection process. Substandard goods have many damaged places. The problem mostly comes from the knot. Foreign pine materials with knots cannot be used for decoration. However, some people often like to be greedy for cheap. They buy a large batch of substandard goods at low prices for decoration. As a result, things happen where small gains are lost. First. Carpenters must waste a selection effort. Second. Chop off the place of the knot. This kind of "waste of time and materials" uneconomical method is the most unworthy. However, this kind of substandard goods is excellent for making cement shells.

Workbench - The long bench on which carpenters do work is collectively called a workbench.

Foot soaking - For city houses built on three floors, the bottom part can sometimes reduce pressure, so there is no need to use large bottom foot materials. Then. It is bound to increase the pier of the pillars. It seems that this is a certain principle. No matter what is accompanied by something, the larger the foot, the higher the height of its upper body. The part where this pier and the pillar body are connected is called foot soaking (Buttess)

Cap - There is another piece of cement board two or three inches thick on top of the parapet wall (Purapet), chimney top, etc. This is the cap. (Apitel)

Jump mouth - The area of the gutter (Gutter) is relatively wide, so the distance of the jump mouth is large. But what part does this jump mouth refer to? That is the place of the outer angle. Almost sophisticated houses. When plasterers do line feet, they often feel extremely difficult because of pulling horses.

Filler - What is called filler (Plate)? It is a kind of thin piece of foreign pine and other materials used to fill up the mark of an insufficient size of the same equipment.

Design of Outdoor Swimming Pools 240

— Xiao Ang

The weather is gradually becoming hot, and the ladies of Shanghai feel a special enthusiasm and need for swimming. Indeed, swimming is one of the best forms of exercise. It can train your body and relieve the heat and boredom. However, in a place like Shanghai, people who love swimming often feel the lack of swimming pools and the carelessness of the facilities. It is true that swimming in China has only been promoted in recent years, so it is no wonder that architects have neglected its design. However, looking at the current trend, the construction of swimming pools will definitely increase year by year, and their design must be improved day by day. The Royal Institute of British Architects once published a paper detailing the design of outdoor swimming pools, which is very detailed. Let me introduce it briefly.

(1) Site Selection

The most important issue in choosing the location of an outdoor swimming pool is the water supply. Some take water from the sea, others from waterworks or wells. In short, the source must be abundant and the quality clean. If it is a seaside swimming pool, the closer to the seaside, the better, because the water supply will be much more convenient. The seating for spectators may be larger and higher, so that those who have finished swimming can enjoy the taste of the sea and the sky. If it is an inland outdoor swimming pool, there must be green lawns, tennis courts, and sports fields around it. The best location is in a park. There is one in Hongkou Park in Shanghai, and other parks should also have one.

(2) Buildings

A. The office should have a ticket office

B. The locker room should have a locker for men and women.

C. One toilet for men and women.

D. Bathing room: Before swimming, you must wash your whole body with warm water to avoid catching a cold and to keep the pool clean. One for men and one for women.

E. Swimming pool, F. Coffee shop, etc. for swimmers to rest

G. Stands for competitions

(3) Swimming Pool Design

The smallest swimming pool must be 25 meters long and 10 meters wide. The largest swimming pool is 100 meters long and 50 meters wide. One-third of the length is very shallow for children and beginners. Two-thirds of the length is a bit deeper, with the deepest part being three to five meters.

Most swimming pools are made of reinforced concrete and painted with white cement on all sides, because this kind of construction is impermeable to water. Many swimming pools are plastered around with colored cement and marble fragments. This kind of architecture is the most magnificent.

On one side of the swimming pool, there should be a ladder every ten meters for entering and exiting the pool.

The diving board should be placed at the deepest end of the water. Most of them are made of elastic wood and covered with palm felt to prevent slipping.
